mklmt10{_}827{_}I was born when Madame Pele" (the Fire Goddess or Volcano Goddess) "became angry with the people of Paiea because they sacrificed no fish to her from their fish-pool, and she sent down a flow of lava from Huulalai and filled up their pond.
mklmt10{_}828{_}For ever was the fish-pond of Paiea filled up.
mklmt10{_}829{_}That was when I was born."
mklmt10{_}830{_}"That was in 1801, when James Boyd was building ships for Kamehameha at Hilo," Pool cast back through the calendar; "which makes you seventy-nine, or eight years older than I.
mklmt10{_}831{_}You are very old."
mklmt10{_}832{_}"Yes, Kanaka Oolea," muttered Kumuhana, pathetically attempting to swell his shrunken chest with pride.
mklmt10{_}833{_}"And you are very wise."
mklmt10{_}834{_}"Yes, Kanaka Oolea."
mklmt10{_}835{_}"And you know many of the secret things that are known only to old men."
mklmt10{_}836{_}"Yes, Kanaka Oolea."
mklmt10{_}837{_}"And then you know--" Hardman Pool broke off, the more effectively to impress and hypnotize the other ancient with the set stare of his pale-washed blue eyes.
mklmt10{_}838{_}"They say the bones of Kahekili were taken from their hiding-place and lie to-day in the Royal Mausoleum.
mklmt10{_}839{_}I have heard it whispered that you alone of all living men truly know."
mklmt10{_}840{_}"I know," was the proud answer.
mklmt10{_}841{_}"I alone know."
mklmt10{_}842{_}"Well, do they lie there?
mklmt10{_}843{_}Yes or no?"
mklmt10{_}844{_}"Kahekili was an alii" (high chief).
mklmt10{_}845{_}"It is from this straight line that your wife Kalama came.
mklmt10{_}846{_}She is an alii."
mklmt10{_}847{_}The old retainer paused and pursed his lean lips in meditation.
mklmt10{_}848{_}"I belong to her, as all my people before me belonged to her people before her.
mklmt10{_}849{_}She only can command the great secrets of me.
mklmt10{_}850{_}She is wise, too wise ever to command me to speak this secret.
mklmt10{_}851{_}To you, O Kanaka Oolea, I do not answer yes, I do not answer no.
mklmt10{_}852{_}This is a secret of the aliis that even the aliis do not know."
mklmt10{_}853{_}"Very good, Kumuhana," Hardman Pool commanded.
mklmt10{_}854{_}"Yet do you forget that I am an alii, and that what my good Kalama does not dare ask, I command to ask.
mklmt10{_}855{_}I can send for her, now, and tell her to command your answer.
mklmt10{_}856{_}But such would be a foolishness unless you prove yourself doubly foolish.
mklmt10{_}857{_}Tell me the secret, and she will never know.
mklmt10{_}858{_}A woman's lips must pour out whatever flows in through her ears, being so made.
mklmt10{_}859{_}I am a man, and man is differently made.
mklmt10{_}860{_}As you well know, my lips suck tight on secrets as a squid sucks to the salty rock.
mklmt10{_}861{_}If you will not tell me alone, then will you tell Kalama and me together, and her lips will talk, her lips will talk, so that the latest malahini will shortly know what, otherwise, you and I alone will know."
mklmt10{_}862{_}Long time Kumuhana sat on in silence, debating the argument and finding no way to evade the fact-logic of it.
mklmt10{_}863{_}"Great is your haole wisdom," he conceded at last.
mklmt10{_}864{_}"Yes?
mklmt10{_}865{_}or no?"
mklmt10{_}866{_}Hardman Pool drove home the point of his steel.
mklmt10{_}867{_}Kumuhana looked about him first, then slowly let his eyes come to rest on the fly-flapping maid.
mklmt10{_}868{_}"Go," Pool commanded her.
mklmt10{_}869{_}"And come not back without you hear a clapping of my hands."
mklmt10{_}870{_}Hardman Pool spoke no further, even after the flapper had disappeared into the house; yet his face adamantly looked:  "Yes or no?"
mklmt10{_}871{_}Again Kumuhana looked carefully about him, and up into the monkey- pod boughs as if to apprehend a lurking listener.
mklmt10{_}872{_}His lips were very dry.
mklmt10{_}873{_}With his tongue he moistened them repeatedly.
mklmt10{_}874{_}Twice he essayed to speak, but was inarticulately husky.
mklmt10{_}875{_}And finally, with bowed head, he whispered, so low and solemnly that Hardman Pool bent his own head to hear:  "No."
mklmt10{_}876{_}Pool clapped his hands, and the little maid ran out of the house to him in tremulous, fluttery haste.
mklmt10{_}877{_}"Bring a milk and gin for old Kumuhana, here," Pool commanded; and, to Kumuhana:  "Now tell me the whole story."
mklmt10{_}878{_}"Wait," was the answer.
mklmt10{_}879{_}"Wait till the little wahine has come and gone."
mklmt10{_}880{_}And when the maid was gone, and the gin and milk had travelled the way predestined of gin and milk when mixed together, Hardman Pool waited without further urge for the story.
mklmt10{_}881{_}Kumuhana pressed his hand to his chest and coughed hollowly at intervals, bidding for encouragement; but in the end, of himself, spoke out.
mklmt10{_}882{_}"It was a terrible thing in the old days when a great alii died.
mklmt10{_}883{_}Kahekili was a great alii.
mklmt10{_}884{_}He might have been king had he lived.
mklmt10{_}885{_}Who can tell?
mklmt10{_}886{_}I was a young man, not yet married.
mklmt10{_}887{_}You know, Kanaka Oolea, when Kahekili died, and you can tell me how old I was.
mklmt10{_}888{_}He died when Governor Boki ran the Blonde Hotel here in Honolulu.
mklmt10{_}889{_}You have heard?"
mklmt10{_}890{_}"I was still on windward Hawaii," Pool answered.
mklmt10{_}891{_}"But I have heard.
mklmt10{_}892{_}Boki made a distillery, and leased Manoa lands to grow sugar for it, and Kaahumanu, who was regent, cancelled the lease, rooted out the cane, and planted potatoes.
mklmt10{_}893{_}And Boki was angry, and prepared to make war, and gathered his fighting men, with a dozen whaleship deserters and five brass six-pounders, out at Waikiki--"  "That was the very time Kahekili died," Kumuhana broke in eagerly.
mklmt10{_}894{_}"You are very wise.
mklmt10{_}895{_}You know many things of the old days better than we old kanakas."
mklmt10{_}896{_}"It was 1829," Pool continued complacently.
mklmt10{_}897{_}"You were twenty-eight years old, and I was twenty, just coming ashore in the open boat after the burning of the Black Prince."
mklmt10{_}898{_}"I was twenty-eight," Kumuhana resumed.
mklmt10{_}899{_}"It sounds right.
mklmt10{_}900{_}I remember well Boki's brass guns at Waikiki.
mklmt10{_}901{_}Kahekili died, too, at the time, at Waikiki.
mklmt10{_}902{_}The people to this day believe his bones were taken to the Hale o Keawe" (mausoleum) "at Honaunau, in Kona-- "  "And long afterward were brought to the Royal Mausoleum here in Honolulu," Pool supplemented.
mklmt10{_}903{_}"Also, Kanaka Oolea, there are some who believe to this day that Queen Alice has them stored with the rest of her ancestral bones in the big jars in her taboo room.
mklmt10{_}904{_}All are wrong.
mklmt10{_}905{_}I know.
mklmt10{_}906{_}The sacred bones of Kahekili are gone and for ever gone.
mklmt10{_}907{_}They rest nowhere.
mklmt10{_}908{_}They have ceased to be.
mklmt10{_}909{_}And many kona winds have whitened the surf at Waikiki since the last man looked upon the last of Kahekili.
mklmt10{_}910{_}I alone remain alive of those men.
mklmt10{_}911{_}I am the last man, and I was not glad to be at the finish.
mklmt10{_}912{_}"For see!
mklmt10{_}913{_}I was a young man, and my heart was white-hot lava for Malia, who was in Kahekili's household.
mklmt10{_}914{_}So was Anapuni's heart white-hot for her, though the colour of his heart was black, as you shall see.
mklmt10{_}915{_}We were at a drinking that night--Anapuni and I--the night that Kahekili died.
mklmt10{_}916{_}Anapuni and I were only commoners, as were all of us kanakas and wahines who were at the drinking with the common sailors and whaleship men from before the mast.
mklmt10{_}917{_}We were drinking on the mats by the beach at Waikiki, close to the old heiau" (temple) "that is not far from what is now the Wilders' beach place.
mklmt10{_}918{_}I learned then and for ever what quantities of drink haole sailormen can stand.
mklmt10{_}919{_}As for us kanakas, our heads were hot and light and rattly as dry gourds with the whisky and the rum.
mklmt10{_}920{_}"It was past midnight, I remember well, when I saw Malia, whom never had I seen at a drinking, come across the wet-hard sand of the beach.
mklmt10{_}921{_}My brain burned like red cinders of hell as I looked upon Anapuni look upon her, he being nearest to her by being across from me in the drinking circle.
mklmt10{_}922{_}Oh, I know it was whisky and rum and youth that made the heat of me; but there, in that moment, the mad mind of me resolved, if she spoke to him and yielded to dance with him first, that I would put both my hands around his throat and throw him down and under the wahine surf there beside us, and drown and choke out his life and the obstacle of him that stood between me and her.
mklmt10{_}923{_}For know, that she had never decided between us, and it was because of him that she was not already and long since mine.
mklmt10{_}924{_}"She was a grand young woman with a body generous as that of a chiefess and more wonderful, as she came upon us, across the wet sand, in the shimmer of the moonlight.
mklmt10{_}925{_}Even the haole sailormen made pause of silence, and with open mouths stared upon her.
mklmt10{_}926{_}Her walk!
mklmt10{_}927{_}I have heard you talk, O Kanaka Oolea, of the woman Helen who caused the war of Troy.
mklmt10{_}928{_}I say of Malia that more men would have stormed the walls of hell for her than went against that old- time city of which it is your custom to talk over much and long when you have drunk too little milk and too much gin.
mklmt10{_}929{_}"Her walk!
mklmt10{_}930{_}In the moonlight there, the soft glow-fire of the jelly-fishes in the surf like the kerosene-lamp footlights I have seen in the new haole theatre!
mklmt10{_}931{_}It was not the walk of a girl, but a woman.
mklmt10{_}932{_}She did not flutter forward like rippling wavelets on a reef-sheltered, placid beach.
mklmt10{_}933{_}There was that in her manner of walk that was big and queenlike, like the motion of the forces of nature, like the rhythmic flow of lava down the slopes of Kau to the sea, like the movement of the huge orderly trade-wind seas, like the rise and fall of the four great tides of the year that may be like music in the eternal ear of God, being too slow of occurrence in time to make a tune for ordinary quick-pulsing, brief-living, swift-dying man.
mklmt10{_}934{_}"Anapuni was nearest.
mklmt10{_}935{_}But she looked at me.
mklmt10{_}936{_}Have you ever heard a call, Kanaka Oolea, that is without sound yet is louder than the conches of God?
mklmt10{_}937{_}So called she to me across that circle of the drinking.
mklmt10{_}938{_}I half arose, for I was not yet full drunken; but Anapuni's arm caught her and drew her, and I sank back on my elbow and watched and raged.
mklmt10{_}939{_}He was for making her sit beside him, and I waited.
mklmt10{_}940{_}Did she sit, and, next, dance with him, I knew that ere morning Anapuni would be a dead man, choked and drowned by me in the shallow surf.
mklmt10{_}941{_}"Strange, is it not, Kanaka Oolea, all this heat called 'love'?
mklmt10{_}942{_}Yet it is not strange.
mklmt10{_}943{_}It must be so in the time of one's youth, else would mankind not go on."
mklmt10{_}944{_}"That is why the desire of woman must be greater than the desire of life," Pool concurred.
mklmt10{_}945{_}"Else would there be neither men nor women."
mklmt10{_}946{_}"Yes," said Kumuhana.
mklmt10{_}947{_}"But it is many a year now since the last of such heat has gone out of me.
mklmt10{_}948{_}I remember it as one remembers an old sunrise--a thing that was.
mklmt10{_}949{_}And so one grows old, and cold, and drinks gin, not for madness, but for warmth.
mklmt10{_}950{_}And the milk is very nourishing.
mklmt10{_}951{_}"But Malia did not sit beside him.
mklmt10{_}952{_}I remember her eyes were wild, her hair down and flying, as she bent over him and whispered in his ear.
mklmt10{_}953{_}And her hair covered him about and hid him as she whispered, and the sight of it pounded my heart against my ribs and dizzied my head till scarcely could I half-see.
mklmt10{_}954{_}And I willed myself with all the will of me that if, in short minutes, she did not come over to me, I would go across the circle and get her.
mklmt10{_}955{_}"It was one of the things never to be.
mklmt10{_}956{_}You remember Chief Konukalani?
mklmt10{_}957{_}Himself he strode up to the circle.
mklmt10{_}958{_}His face was black with anger.
mklmt10{_}959{_}He gripped Malia, not by the arm, but by the hair, and dragged her away behind him and was gone.
mklmt10{_}960{_}Of that, even now, can I understand not the half.
mklmt10{_}961{_}I, who was for slaying Anapuni because of her, raised neither hand nor voice of protest when Konukalani dragged her away by the hair--nor did Anapuni.
mklmt10{_}962{_}Of course, we were common men, and he was a chief.
mklmt10{_}963{_}That I know.
mklmt10{_}964{_}But why should two common men, mad with desire of woman, with desire of woman stronger in them than desire of life, let any one chief, even the highest in the land, drag the woman away by the hair?
mklmt10{_}965{_}Desiring her more than life, why should the two men fear to slay then and immediately the one chief?
mklmt10{_}966{_}Here is something stronger than life, stronger than woman, but what is it?
mklmt10{_}967{_}and why?"
mklmt10{_}968{_}"I will answer you," said Hardman Pool.
mklmt10{_}969{_}"It is so because most men are fools, and therefore must be taken care of by the few men who are wise.
mklmt10{_}970{_}Such is the secret of chiefship.
mklmt10{_}971{_}In all the world are chiefs over men.
mklmt10{_}972{_}In all the world that has been have there ever been chiefs, who must say to the many fool men:  'Do this; do not do that.
mklmt10{_}973{_}Work, and work as we tell you or your bellies will remain empty and you will perish.
mklmt10{_}974{_}Obey the laws we set you or you will be beasts and without place in the world.
mklmt10{_}975{_}You would not have been, save for the chiefs before you who ordered and regulated for your fathers.
mklmt10{_}976{_}No seed of you will come after you, except that we order and regulate for you now.
mklmt10{_}977{_}You must be peace-abiding, and decent, and blow your noses.
mklmt10{_}978{_}You must be early to bed of nights, and up early in the morning to work if you would heave beds to sleep in and not roost in trees like the silly fowls.
mklmt10{_}979{_}This is the season for the yam-planting and you must plant now.
mklmt10{_}980{_}We say now, to-day, and not picnicking and hulaing to-day and yam-planting to-morrow or some other day of the many careless days.
mklmt10{_}981{_}You must not kill one another, and you must leave your neighbours' wives alone.
mklmt10{_}982{_}All this is life for you, because you think but one day at a time, while we, your chiefs, think for you all days and for days ahead.'"
mklmt10{_}983{_}"Like a cloud on the mountain-top that comes down and wraps about you and that you dimly see is a cloud, so is your wisdom to me, Kanaka Oolea," Kumuhana murmured.
mklmt10{_}984{_}"Yet is it sad that I should be born a common man and live all my days a common man."
mklmt10{_}985{_}"That is because you were of yourself common," Hardman Pool assured him.
mklmt10{_}986{_}"When a man is born common, and is by nature uncommon, he rises up and overthrows the chiefs and makes himself chief over the chiefs.
mklmt10{_}987{_}Why do you not run my ranch, with its many thousands of cattle, and shift the pastures by the rain-fall, and pick the bulls, and arrange the bargaining and the selling of the meat to the sailing ships and war vessels and the people who live in the Honolulu houses, and fight with lawyers, and help make laws, and even tell the King what is wise for him to do and what is dangerous?
mklmt10{_}988{_}Why does not any man do this that I do?
mklmt10{_}989{_}Any man of all the men who work for me, feed out of my hand, and let me do their thinking for them--me, who work harder than any of them, who eats no more than any of them, and who can sleep on no more than one lauhala mat at a time like any of them?"
mklmt10{_}990{_}"I am out of the cloud, Kanaka Oolea," said Kumuhana, with a visible brightening of countenance.
mklmt10{_}991{_}"More clearly do I see.
mklmt10{_}992{_}All my long years have the aliis I was born under thought for me.
mklmt10{_}993{_}Ever, when I was hungry, I came to them for food, as I come to your kitchen now.
mklmt10{_}994{_}Many people eat in your kitchen, and the days of feasts when you slay fat steers for all of us are understandable.
mklmt10{_}995{_}It is why I come to you this day, an old man whose labour of strength is not worth a shilling a week, and ask of you twelve dollars to buy a jackass and a second-hand saddle and bridle.
mklmt10{_}996{_}It is why twice ten fool men of us, under these monkey-pods half an hour ago, asked of you a dollar or two, or four or five, or ten or twelve.
mklmt10{_}997{_}We are the careless ones of the careless days who will not plant the yam in season if our alii does not compel us, who will not think one day for ourselves, and who, when we age to worthlessness, know that our alii will think kow-kow into our bellies and a grass thatch over our heads.
mklmt10{_}998{_}Hardman Pool bowed his appreciation, and urged:  "But the bones of Kahekili.
mklmt10{_}999{_}The Chief Konukalani had just dragged away Malia by the hair of the head, and you and Anapuni sat on without protest in the circle of drinking.
mklmt10{_}1000{_}What was it Malia whispered in Anapuni's ear, bending over him, her hair hiding the face of him?"
mklmt10{_}1001{_}"That Kahekili was dead.
mklmt10{_}1002{_}That was what she whispered to Anapuni.
mklmt10{_}1003{_}That Kahekili was dead, just dead, and that the chiefs, ordering all within the house to remain within, were debating the disposal of the bones and meat of him before word of his death should get abroad.
mklmt10{_}1004{_}That the high priest Eoppo was deciding them, and that she had overheard no less than Anapuni and me chosen as the sacrifices to go the way of Kahekili and his bones and to care for him afterward and for ever in the shadowy other world."
mklmt10{_}1005{_}"The moepuu, the human sacrifice," Pool commented.
mklmt10{_}1006{_}"Yet it was nine years since the coming of the missionaries."
mklmt10{_}1007{_}"And it was the year before their coming that the idols were cast down and the taboos broken," Kumuhana added.
mklmt10{_}1008{_}"But the chiefs still practised the old ways, the custom of hunakele, and hid the bones of the aliis where no men should find them and make fish-hooks of their jaws or arrow heads of their long bones for the slaying of little mice in sport.
mklmt10{_}1009{_}Behold, O Kanaka Oolea!"
mklmt10{_}1010{_}The old man thrust out his tongue; and, to Pool's amazement, he saw the surface of that sensitive organ, from root to tip, tattooed in intricate designs.
mklmt10{_}1011{_}"That was done after the missionaries came, several years afterward, when Keopuolani died.
mklmt10{_}1012{_}Also, did I knock out four of my front teeth, and half-circles did I burn over my body with blazing bark.
mklmt10{_}1013{_}And whoever ventured out-of-doors that night was slain by the chiefs.
mklmt10{_}1014{_}Nor could a light be shown in a house or a whisper of noise be made.
mklmt10{_}1015{_}Even dogs and hogs that made a noise were slain, nor all that night were the ships' bells of the haoles in the harbour allowed to strike.
mklmt10{_}1016{_}It was a terrible thing in those days when an alii died.
mklmt10{_}1017{_}"But the night that Kahekili died.
mklmt10{_}1018{_}We sat on in the drinking circle after Konukalani dragged Malia away by the hair.
mklmt10{_}1019{_}Some of the haole sailors grumbled; but they were few in the land in those days and the kanakas many.
mklmt10{_}1020{_}And never was Malia seen of men again.
mklmt10{_}1021{_}Konukalani alone knew the manner of her slaying, and he never told.
mklmt10{_}1022{_}And in after years what common men like Anapuni and me should dare to question him?
mklmt10{_}1023{_}"Now she had told Anapuni before she was dragged away.
mklmt10{_}1024{_}But Anapuni's heart was black.
mklmt10{_}1025{_}Me he did not tell.
mklmt10{_}1026{_}Worthy he was of the killing I had intended for him.
mklmt10{_}1027{_}There was a giant harpooner in the circle, whose singing was like the bellowing of bulls; and, gazing on him in amazement while he roared some song of the sea, when next I looked across the circle to Anapuni, Anapuni was gone.
mklmt10{_}1028{_}He had fled to the high mountains where he could hide with the bird-catchers a week of moons.
mklmt10{_}1029{_}This I learned afterward.
mklmt10{_}1030{_}"I?
mklmt10{_}1031{_}I sat on, ashamed of my desire of woman that had not been so strong as my slave-obedience to a chief.
mklmt10{_}1032{_}And I drowned my shame in large drinks of rum and whisky, till the world went round and round, inside my head and out, and the Southern Cross danced a hula in the sky, and the Koolau Mountains bowed their lofty summits to Waikiki and the surf of Waikiki kissed them on their brows.
mklmt10{_}1033{_}And the giant harpooner was still roaring, his the last sounds in my ear, as I fell back on the lauhala mat, and was to all things for the time as one dead.
mklmt10{_}1034{_}"When I awoke was at the faint first beginning of dawn.
mklmt10{_}1035{_}I was being kicked by a hard naked heel in the ribs.
mklmt10{_}1036{_}What of the enormousness of the drink I had consumed, the feelings aroused in me by the heel were not pleasant.
mklmt10{_}1037{_}The kanakas and wahines of the drinking were gone.
mklmt10{_}1038{_}I alone remained among the sleeping sailormen, the giant harpooner snoring like a whale, his head upon my feet.
mklmt10{_}1039{_}"More heel-kicks, and I sat up and was sick.
mklmt10{_}1040{_}But the one who kicked was impatient, and demanded to know where was Anapuni.
mklmt10{_}1041{_}And I did not know, and was kicked, this time from both sides by two impatient men, because I did not know.
mklmt10{_}1042{_}Nor did I know that Kahekili was dead.
mklmt10{_}1043{_}Yet did I guess something serious was afoot, for the two men who kicked me were chiefs, and no common men crouched behind them to do their bidding.
mklmt10{_}1044{_}One was Aimoku, of Kaneche; the other Humuhumu, of Manoa.
mklmt10{_}1045{_}"They commanded me to go with them, and they were not kind in their commanding; and as I uprose, the head of the giant harpooner was rolled off my feet, past the edge of the mat, into the sand.
mklmt10{_}1046{_}He grunted like a pig, his lips opened, and all of his tongue rolled out of his mouth into the sand.
mklmt10{_}1047{_}Nor did he draw it back.
mklmt10{_}1048{_}For the first time I knew how long was a man's tongue.
mklmt10{_}1049{_}The sight of the sand on it made me sick for the second time.
mklmt10{_}1050{_}It is a terrible thing, the next day after a night of drinking.
mklmt10{_}1051{_}I was afire, dry afire, all the inside of me like a burnt cinder, like aa lava, like the harpooner's tongue dry and gritty with sand.
mklmt10{_}1052{_}I bent for a half-drunk drinking coconut, but Aimoku kicked it out of my shaking fingers, and Humuhumu smote me with the heel of his hand on my neck.
mklmt10{_}1053{_}"They walked before me, side by side, their faces solemn and black, and I walked at their heels.
mklmt10{_}1054{_}My mouth stank of the drink, and my head was sick with the stale fumes of it, and I would have cut off my right hand for a drink of water, one drink, a mouthful even.
mklmt10{_}1055{_}And, had I had it, I know it would have sizzled in my belly like water spilled on heated stones for the roasting.
mklmt10{_}1056{_}It is terrible, the next day after the drinking.
mklmt10{_}1057{_}All the life-time of many men who died young has passed by me since the last I was able to do such mad drinking of youth when youth knows not capacity and is undeterred.
mklmt10{_}1058{_}"But as we went on, I began to know that some alii was dead.
mklmt10{_}1059{_}No kanakas lay asleep in the sand, nor stole home from their love- making; and no canoes were abroad after the early fish most catchable then inside the reef at the change of the tide.
mklmt10{_}1060{_}When we came, past the hoiau" (temple), "to where the Great Kamehameha used to haul out his brigs and schooners, I saw, under the canoe-sheds, that the mat-thatches of Kahekili's great double canoe had been taken off, and that even then, at low tide, many men were launching it down across the sand into the water.
mklmt10{_}1061{_}But all these men were chiefs.
mklmt10{_}1062{_}And, though my eyes swam, and the inside of my head went around and around, and the inside of my body was a cinder athirst, I guessed that the alii who was dead was Kahekili.
mklmt10{_}1063{_}For he was old, and most likely of the aliis to be dead."
mklmt10{_}1064{_}"It was his death, as I have heard it, more than the intercession of Kekuanaoa, that spoiled Governor Boki's rebellion," Hardman Pool observed.
mklmt10{_}1065{_}"It was Kahekili's death that spoiled it," Kumuhana confirmed.
mklmt10{_}1066{_}"All commoners, when the word slipped out that night of his death, fled into the shelter of the grass houses, nor lighted fire nor pipes, nor breathed loudly, being therein and thereby taboo from use for sacrifice.
mklmt10{_}1067{_}And all Governor Boki's commoners of fighting men, as well as the haole deserters from ships, so fled, so that the brass guns lay unserved and his handful of chiefs of themselves could do nothing.
mklmt10{_}1068{_}"Aimoku and Humuhumu made me sit on the sand to the side from the launching of the great double-canoe.
mklmt10{_}1069{_}And when it was afloat all the chiefs were athirst, not being used to such toil; and I was told to climb the palms beside the canoe-sheds and throw down drink-coconuts.
mklmt10{_}1070{_}They drank and were refreshed, but me they refused to let drink.
mklmt10{_}1071{_}"Then they bore Kahekili from his house to the canoe in a haole coffin, oiled and varnished and new.
mklmt10{_}1072{_}It had been made by a ship's carpenter, who thought he was making a boat that must not leak.
mklmt10{_}1073{_}It was very tight, and over where the face of Kahekili lay was nothing but thin glass.
mklmt10{_}1074{_}The chiefs had not screwed on the outside plank to cover the glass.
mklmt10{_}1075{_}Maybe they did not know the manner of haole coffins; but at any rate I was to be glad they did not know, as you shall see.
mklmt10{_}1076{_}"'There is but one moepuu,' said the priest Eoppo, looking at me where I sat on the coffin in the bottom of the canoe.
mklmt10{_}1077{_}Already the chiefs were paddling out through the reef.
mklmt10{_}1078{_}"'The other has run into hiding,' Aimoku answered.
mklmt10{_}1079{_}'This one was all we could get.'
mklmt10{_}1080{_}"And then I knew.
mklmt10{_}1081{_}I knew everything.
mklmt10{_}1082{_}I was to be sacrificed.
mklmt10{_}1083{_}Anapuni had been planned for the other sacrifice.
mklmt10{_}1084{_}That was what Malia had whispered to Anapuni at the drinking.
mklmt10{_}1085{_}And she had been dragged away before she could tell me.
mklmt10{_}1086{_}And in his blackness of heart he had not told me.
mklmt10{_}1087{_}"'There should be two,' said Eoppo.
mklmt10{_}1088{_}'It is the law.'
mklmt10{_}1089{_}"Aimoku stopped paddling and looked back shoreward as if to return and get a second sacrifice.
mklmt10{_}1090{_}But several of the chiefs contended no, saying that all commoners were fled to the mountains or were lying taboo in their houses, and that it might take days before they could catch one.
mklmt10{_}1091{_}In the end Eoppo gave in, though he grumbled from time to time that the law required two moepuus.
mklmt10{_}1092{_}"We paddled on, past Diamond Head and abreast of Koko Head, till we were in the midway of the Molokai Channel.
mklmt10{_}1093{_}There was quite a sea running, though the trade wind was blowing light.
mklmt10{_}1094{_}The chiefs rested from their paddles, save for the steersmen who kept the canoes bow-on to the wind and swell.
mklmt10{_}1095{_}And, ere they proceeded further in the matter, they opened more coconuts and drank.
mklmt10{_}1096{_}"'I do not mind so much being the moepuu,' I said to Humuhumu; 'but I should like to have a drink before I am slain.'
mklmt10{_}1097{_}I got no drink.
mklmt10{_}1098{_}But I spoke true.
mklmt10{_}1099{_}I was too sick of the much whisky and rum to be afraid to die.
mklmt10{_}1100{_}At least my mouth would stink no more, nor my head ache, nor the inside of me be as dry-hot sand.
mklmt10{_}1101{_}Almost worst of all, I suffered at thought of the harpooner's tongue, as last I had seen it lying on the sand and covered with sand.
mklmt10{_}1102{_}O Kanaka Oolea, what animals young men are with the drink!
mklmt10{_}1103{_}Not until they have grown old, like you and me, do they control their wantonness of thirst and drink sparingly, like you and me."
mklmt10{_}1104{_}"Because we have to," Hardman Pool rejoined.
mklmt10{_}1105{_}"Old stomachs are worn thin and tender, and we drink sparingly because we dare not drink more.
mklmt10{_}1106{_}We are wise, but the wisdom is bitter."
mklmt10{_}1107{_}"The priest Eoppo sang a long mele about Kahekili's mother and his mother's mother, and all their mothers all the way back to the beginning of time," Kumuhana resumed.
mklmt10{_}1108{_}"And it seemed I must die of my sand-hot dryness ere he was done.
mklmt10{_}1109{_}And he called upon all the gods of the under world, the middle world and the over world, to care for and cherish the dead alii about to be consigned to them, and to carry out the curses--they were terrible curses--he laid upon all living men and men to live after who might tamper with the bones of Kahekili to use them in sport of vermin-slaying.
mklmt10{_}1110{_}"Do you know, Kanaka Oolea, the priest talked a language largely different, and I know it was the priest language, the old language.
mklmt10{_}1111{_}Maui he did not name Maui, but Maui-Tiki-Tiki and Maui-Po-Tiki.
mklmt10{_}1112{_}And Hina, the goddess-mother of Maui, he named Ina.
mklmt10{_}1113{_}And Maui's god-father he named sometimes Akalana and sometimes Kanaloa.
mklmt10{_}1114{_}Strange how one about to die and very thirsty should remember such things!
mklmt10{_}1115{_}And I remember the priest named Hawaii as Vaii, and Lanai as Ngangai."
mklmt10{_}1116{_}"Those were the Maori names," Hardman Pool explained, "and the Samoan and Tongan names, that the priests brought with them in their first voyages from the south in the long ago when they found Hawaii and settled to dwell upon it."
mklmt10{_}1117{_}"Great is your wisdom, O Kanaka Oolea," the old man accorded solemnly.
mklmt10{_}1118{_}"Ku, our Supporter of the Heavens, the priest named Tu, and also Ru; and La, our God of the Sun, he named Ra--"  "And Ra was a sun-god in Egypt in the long ago," Pool interrupted with a sparkle of interest.
mklmt10{_}1119{_}"Truly, you Polynesians have travelled far in time and space since first you began.
mklmt10{_}1120{_}A far cry it is from Old Egypt, when Atlantis was still afloat, to Young Hawaii in the North Pacific.
mklmt10{_}1121{_}But proceed, Kumuhana.
mklmt10{_}1122{_}Do you remember anything also of what the priest Eoppo sang?"
mklmt10{_}1123{_}"At the very end," came the confirming nod, "though I was near dead myself, and nearer to die under the priest's knife, he sang what I have remembered every word of.
mklmt10{_}1124{_}Listen!
mklmt10{_}1125{_}It was thus."
mklmt10{_}1126{_}And in quavering falsetto, with the customary broken-notes, the old man sang.
mklmt10{_}1127{_}"A Maori death-chant unmistakable," Pool exclaimed, "sung by an Hawaiian with a tattooed tongue!
mklmt10{_}1128{_}Repeat it once again, and I shall say it to you in English."
mklmt10{_}1129{_}And when it had been repeated, he spoke it slowly in English:   "But death is nothing new.
mklmt10{_}1130{_}Death is and has been ever since old Maui died.
mklmt10{_}1131{_}Then Pata-tai laughed loud And woke the goblin-god, Who severed him in two, and shut him in, So dusk of eve came on."
mklmt10{_}1132{_}"And at the last," Kumuhana resumed, "I was not slain.
mklmt10{_}1133{_}Eoppo, the killing knife in hand and ready to lift for the blow, did not lift.
mklmt10{_}1134{_}And I?
mklmt10{_}1135{_}How did I feel and think?
mklmt10{_}1136{_}Often, Kanaka Oolea, have I since laughed at the memory of it.
mklmt10{_}1137{_}I felt very thirsty.
mklmt10{_}1138{_}I did not want to die.
mklmt10{_}1139{_}I wanted a drink of water.
mklmt10{_}1140{_}I knew I was going to die, and I kept remembering the thousand waterfalls falling to waste down the pans" (precipices) "of the windward Koolau Mountains.
mklmt10{_}1141{_}I did not think of Anapuni.
mklmt10{_}1142{_}I was too thirsty.
mklmt10{_}1143{_}I did not think of Malia.
mklmt10{_}1144{_}I was too thirsty.
mklmt10{_}1145{_}But continually, inside my head, I saw the tongue of the harpooner, covered dry with sand, as I had last seen it, lying in the sand.
mklmt10{_}1146{_}My tongue was like that, too.
mklmt10{_}1147{_}And in the bottom of the canoe rolled about many drinking nuts.
mklmt10{_}1148{_}Yet I did not attempt to drink, for these were chiefs and I was a common man.
mklmt10{_}1149{_}"'No,' said Eoppo, commanding the chiefs to throw overboard the coffin.
mklmt10{_}1150{_}'There are not two moepuus, therefore there shall be none.'
mklmt10{_}1151{_}"'Slay the one,' the chiefs cried.
mklmt10{_}1152{_}"But Eoppo shook his head, and said:  'We cannot send Kahekili on his way with only the tops of the taro.'
mklmt10{_}1153{_}"'Half a fish is better than none,' Aimoku said the old saying.
mklmt10{_}1154{_}"'Not at the burying of an alii,' was the priest's quick reply.
mklmt10{_}1155{_}'It is the law.
mklmt10{_}1156{_}We cannot be niggard with Kahekili and cut his allotment of sacrifice in half.'
mklmt10{_}1157{_}"So, for the moment, while the coffin went overside, I was not slain.
mklmt10{_}1158{_}And it was strange that I was glad immediately that I was to live.
mklmt10{_}1159{_}And I began to remember Malia, and to begin to plot a vengeance on Anapuni.
mklmt10{_}1160{_}And with the blood of life thus freshening in me, my thirst multiplied on itself tenfold and my tongue and mouth and throat seemed as sanded as the tongue of the harpooner.
mklmt10{_}1161{_}The coffin being overboard, I was sitting in the bottom of the canoe.
mklmt10{_}1162{_}A coconut rolled between my legs and I closed them on it.
mklmt10{_}1163{_}But as I picked it up in my hand, Aimoku smote my hand with the paddle-edge.
mklmt10{_}1164{_}Behold!"
mklmt10{_}1165{_}He held up the hand, showing two fingers crooked from never having been set.
mklmt10{_}1166{_}"I had no time to vex over my pain, for worse things were upon me.
mklmt10{_}1167{_}All the chiefs were crying out in horror.
mklmt10{_}1168{_}The coffin, head-end up, had not sunk.
mklmt10{_}1169{_}It bobbed up and down in the sea astern of us.
mklmt10{_}1170{_}And the canoe, without way on it, bow-on to sea and wind, was drifted down by sea and wind upon the coffin.
mklmt10{_}1171{_}And the glass of it was to us, so that we could see the face and head of Kahekili through the glass; and he grinned at us through the glass and seemed alive already in the other world and angry with us, and, with other-world power, about to wreak his anger upon us.
mklmt10{_}1172{_}Up and down he bobbed, and the canoe drifted closer upon him.
mklmt10{_}1173{_}"'Kill him!'
mklmt10{_}1174{_}'Bleed him!'
mklmt10{_}1175{_}'Thrust to the heart of him!'
mklmt10{_}1176{_}These things the chiefs were crying out to Eoppo in their fear.
mklmt10{_}1177{_}'Over with the taro tops!'
mklmt10{_}1178{_}'Let the alii have the half of a fish!'
mklmt10{_}1179{_}"Eoppo, priest though he was, was likewise afraid, and his reason weakened before the sight of Kahekili in his haole coffin that would not sink.
mklmt10{_}1180{_}He seized me by the hair, drew me to my feet, and lifted the knife to plunge to my heart.
mklmt10{_}1181{_}And there was no resistance in me.
mklmt10{_}1182{_}I knew again only that I was very thirsty, and before my swimming eyes, in mid-air and close up, dangled the sanded tongue of the harpooner.
mklmt10{_}1183{_}"But before the knife could fall and drive in, the thing happened that saved me.
mklmt10{_}1184{_}Akai, half-brother to Governor Boki, as you will remember, was steersman of the canoe, and, therefore, in the stern, was nearest to the coffin and its dead that would not sink.
mklmt10{_}1185{_}He was wild with fear, and he thrust out with the point of his paddle to fend off the coffined alii that seemed bent to come on board.
mklmt10{_}1186{_}The point of the paddle struck the glass.
mklmt10{_}1187{_}The glass broke--"  "And the coffin immediately sank," Hardman Pool broke in; "the air that floated it escaping through the broken glass."
mklmt10{_}1188{_}"The coffin immediately sank, being builded by the ship's carpenter like a boat," Kumuhana confirmed.
mklmt10{_}1189{_}"And I, who was a moepuu, became a man once more.
mklmt10{_}1190{_}And I lived, though I died a thousand deaths from thirst before we gained back to the beach at Waikiki.
mklmt10{_}1191{_}"And so, O Kanaka Oolea, the bones of Kahekili do not lie in the Royal Mausoleum.
mklmt10{_}1192{_}They are at the bottom of Molokai Channel, if not, long since, they have become floating dust of slime, or, builded into the bodies of the coral creatures dead and gone, are builded into the coral reef itself.
mklmt10{_}1193{_}Of men I am the one living who saw the bones of Kahekili sink into the Molokai Channel."
mklmt10{_}1194{_}In the pause that followed, wherein Hardman Pool was deep sunk in meditation, Kumuhana licked his dry lips many times.
mklmt10{_}1195{_}At the last he broke silence:  "The twelve dollars, Kanaka Oolea, for the jackass and the second- hand saddle and bridle?"
mklmt10{_}1196{_}"The twelve dollars would be thine," Pool responded, passing to the ancient one six dollars and a half, "save that I have in my stable junk the very bridle and saddle for you which I shall give you.
mklmt10{_}1197{_}These six dollars and a half will buy you the perfectly suitable jackass of the pake" (Chinese) "at Kokako who told me only yesterday that such was the price."
mklmt10{_}1198{_}They sat on, Pool meditating, conning over and over to himself the Maori death-chant he had heard, and especially the line, "So dusk of eve came on," finding in it an intense satisfaction of beauty; Kumuhana licking his lips and tokening that he waited for something more.
mklmt10{_}1199{_}At last he broke silence.
mklmt10{_}1200{_}"I have talked long, O Kanaka Oolea.
mklmt10{_}1201{_}There is not the enduring moistness in my mouth that was when I was young.
mklmt10{_}1202{_}It seems that afresh upon me is the thirst that was mine when tormented by the visioned tongue of the harpooner.
mklmt10{_}1203{_}The gin and milk is very good, O Kanaka Oolea, for a tongue that is like the harpooner's."
mklmt10{_}1204{_}A shadow of a smile flickered across Pool's face.
mklmt10{_}1205{_}He clapped his hands, and the little maid came running.
mklmt10{_}1206{_}"Bring one glass of gin and milk for old Kumuhana," commanded Hardman Pool.
mklmt10{_}1207{_}WAIKIKI, HONOLULU June 28, 1916.
mklmt10{_}1208{_}WHEN ALICE TOLD HER SOUL    This, of Alice Akana, is an affair of Hawaii, not of this day, but of days recent enough, when Abel Ah Yo preached his famous revival in Honolulu and persuaded Alice Akana to tell her soul.
mklmt10{_}1209{_}But what Alice told concerned itself with the earlier history of the then surviving generation.
mklmt10{_}1210{_}For Alice Akana was fifty years old, had begun life early, and, early and late, lived it spaciously.
mklmt10{_}1211{_}What she knew went back into the roots and foundations of families, businesses, and plantations.
mklmt10{_}1212{_}She was the one living repository of accurate information that lawyers sought out, whether the information they required related to land-boundaries and land gifts, or to marriages, births, bequests, or scandals.
mklmt10{_}1213{_}Rarely, because of the tight tongue she kept behind her teeth, did she give them what they asked; and when she did was when only equity was served and no one was hurt.
mklmt10{_}1214{_}For Alice had lived, from early in her girlhood, a life of flowers, and song, and wine, and dance; and, in her later years, had herself been mistress of these revels by office of mistress of the hula house.
mklmt10{_}1215{_}In such atmosphere, where mandates of God and man and caution are inhibited, and where woozled tongues will wag, she acquired her historical knowledge of things never otherwise whispered and rarely guessed.
mklmt10{_}1216{_}And her tight tongue had served her well, so that, while the old-timers knew she must know, none ever heard her gossip of the times of Kalakaua's boathouse, nor of the high times of officers of visiting warships, nor of the diplomats and ministers and councils of the countries of the world.
mklmt10{_}1217{_}So, at fifty, loaded with historical dynamite sufficient, if it were ever exploded, to shake the social and commercial life of the Islands, still tight of tongue, Alice Akana was mistress of the hula house, manageress of the dancing girls who hula'd for royalty, for luaus (feasts), house-parties, poi suppers, and curious tourists.
mklmt10{_}1218{_}And, at fifty, she was not merely buxom, but short and fat in the Polynesian peasant way, with a constitution and lack of organic weakness that promised incalculable years.
mklmt10{_}1219{_}But it was at fifty that she strayed, quite by chance of time and curiosity, into Abel Ah Yo's revival meeting.
mklmt10{_}1220{_}Now Abel Ah Yo, in his theology and word wizardry, was as much mixed a personage as Billy Sunday.
mklmt10{_}1221{_}In his genealogy he was much more mixed, for he was compounded of one-fourth Portuguese, one- fourth Scotch, one-fourth Hawaiian, and one-fourth Chinese.
mklmt10{_}1222{_}The Pentecostal fire he flamed forth was hotter and more variegated than could any one of the four races of him alone have flamed forth.
mklmt10{_}1223{_}For in him were gathered together the cannyness and the cunning, the wit and the wisdom, the subtlety and the rawness, the passion and the philosophy, the agonizing spirit-groping and he legs up to the knees in the dung of reality, of the four radically different breeds that contributed to the sum of him.
mklmt10{_}1224{_}His, also, was the clever self-deceivement of the entire clever compound.
mklmt10{_}1225{_}When it came to word wizardry, he had Billy Sunday, master of slang and argot of one language, skinned by miles.
mklmt10{_}1226{_}For in Abel Ah Yo were the five verbs, and nouns, and adjectives, and metaphors of four living languages.
mklmt10{_}1227{_}Intermixed and living promiscuously and vitally together, he possessed in these languages a reservoir of expression in which a myriad Billy Sundays could drown.
mklmt10{_}1228{_}Of no race, a mongrel par excellence, a heterogeneous scrabble, the genius of the admixture was superlatively Abel Ah Yo's.
mklmt10{_}1229{_}Like a chameleon, he titubated and scintillated grandly between the diverse parts of him, stunning by frontal attack and surprising and confouding by flanking sweeps the mental homogeneity of the more simply constituted souls who came in to his revival to sit under him and flame to his flaming.
mklmt10{_}1230{_}Abel Ah Yo believed in himself and his mixedness, as he believed in the mixedness of his weird concept that God looked as much like him as like any man, being no mere tribal god, but a world god that must look equally like all races of all the world, even if it led to piebaldness.
mklmt10{_}1231{_}And the concept worked.
mklmt10{_}1232{_}Chinese, Korean, Japanese, Hawaiian, Porto Rican, Russian, English, French--members of all races--knelt without friction, side by side, to his revision of deity.
mklmt10{_}1233{_}Himself in his tender youth an apostate to the Church of England, Abel Ah Yo had for years suffered the lively sense of being a Judas sinner.
mklmt10{_}1234{_}Essentially religious, he had foresworn the Lord.
mklmt10{_}1235{_}Like Judas therefore he was.
mklmt10{_}1236{_}Judas was damned.
mklmt10{_}1237{_}Wherefore he, Abel Ah Yo, was damned; and he did not want to be damned.
mklmt10{_}1238{_}So, quite after the manner of humans, he squirmed and twisted to escape damnation.
mklmt10{_}1239{_}The day came when he solved his escape.
mklmt10{_}1240{_}The doctrine that Judas was damned, he concluded, was a misinterpretation of God, who, above all things, stood for justice.
mklmt10{_}1241{_}Judas had been God's servant, specially selected to perform a particularly nasty job.
mklmt10{_}1242{_}Therefore Judas, ever faithful, a betrayer only by divine command, was a saint.
mklmt10{_}1243{_}Ergo, he, Abel Ah Yo, was a saint by very virtue of his apostasy to a particular sect, and he could have access with clear grace any time to God.
mklmt10{_}1244{_}This theory became one of the major tenets of his preaching, and was especially efficacious in cleansing the consciences of the back-sliders from all other faiths who else, in the secrecy of their subconscious selves, were being crushed by the weight of the Judas sin.
mklmt10{_}1245{_}To Abel Ah Yo, God's plan was as clear as if he, Abel Ah Yo, had planned it himself.
mklmt10{_}1246{_}All would be saved in the end, although some took longer than others, and would win only to backseats.
mklmt10{_}1247{_}Man's place in the ever-fluxing chaos of the world was definite and pre-ordained--if by no other token, then by denial that there was any ever-fluxing chaos.
mklmt10{_}1248{_}This was a mere bugbear of mankind's addled fancy; and, by stinging audacities of thought and speech, by vivid slang that bit home by sheerest intimacy into his listeners' mental processes, he drove the bugbear from their brains, showed them the loving clarity of God's design, and, thereby, induced in them spiritual serenity and calm.
mklmt10{_}1249{_}What chance had Alice Akana, herself pure and homogeneous Hawaiian, against his subtle, democratic-tinged, four-race-engendered, slang- munitioned attack?
mklmt10{_}1250{_}He knew, by contact, almost as much as she about the waywardness of living and sinning--having been singing boy on the passenger-ships between Hawaii and California, and, after that, bar boy, afloat and ashore, from the Barbary Coast to Heinie's Tavern.
mklmt10{_}1251{_}In point of fact, he had left his job of Number One Bar Boy at the University Club to embark on his great preachment revival.
mklmt10{_}1252{_}So, when Alice Akana strayed in to scoff, she remained to pray to Abel Ah Yo's god, who struck her hard-headed mind as the most sensible god of which she had ever heard.
mklmt10{_}1253{_}She gave money into Abel Ah Yo's collection plate, closed up the hula house, and dismissed the hula dancers to more devious ways of earning a livelihood, shed her bright colours and raiments and flower garlands, and bought a Bible.
mklmt10{_}1254{_}It was a time of religious excitement in the purlieus of Honolulu.
mklmt10{_}1255{_}The thing was a democratic movement of the people toward God.
mklmt10{_}1256{_}Place and caste were invited, but never came.
mklmt10{_}1257{_}The stupid lowly, and the humble lowly, only, went down on its knees at the penitent form, admitted its pathological weight and hurt of sin, eliminated and purged all its bafflements, and walked forth again upright under the sun, child-like and pure, upborne by Abel Ah Yo's god's arm around it.
mklmt10{_}1258{_}In short, Abel Ah Yo's revival was a clearing house for sin and sickness of spirit, wherein sinners were relieved of their burdens and made light and bright and spiritually healthy again.
mklmt10{_}1259{_}But Alice was not happy.
mklmt10{_}1260{_}She had not been cleared.
mklmt10{_}1261{_}She bought and dispersed Bibles, contributed more money to the plate, contralto'd gloriously in all the hymns, but would not tell her soul.
mklmt10{_}1262{_}In vain Abel Ah Yo wrestled with her.
mklmt10{_}1263{_}She would not go down on her knees at the penitent form and voice the things of tarnish within her-- the ill things of good friends of the old days.
mklmt10{_}1264{_}"You cannot serve two masters," Abel Ah Yo told her.
mklmt10{_}1265{_}"Hell is full of those who have tried.
mklmt10{_}1266{_}Single of heart and pure of heart must you make your peace with God.
mklmt10{_}1267{_}Not until you tell your soul to God right out in meeting will you be ready for redemption.
mklmt10{_}1268{_}In the meantime you will suffer the canker of the sin you carry about within you."
mklmt10{_}1269{_}Scientifically, though he did not know it and though he continually jeered at science, Abel Ah Yo was right.
mklmt10{_}1270{_}Not could she be again as a child and become radiantly clad in God's grace, until she had eliminated from her soul, by telling, all the sophistications that had been hers, including those she shared with others.
mklmt10{_}1271{_}In the Protestant way, she must bare her soul in public, as in the Catholic way it was done in the privacy of the confessional.
mklmt10{_}1272{_}The result of such baring would be unity, tranquillity, happiness, cleansing, redemption, and immortal life.
mklmt10{_}1273{_}"Choose!"
mklmt10{_}1274{_}Abel Ah Yo thundered.
mklmt10{_}1275{_}"Loyalty to God, or loyalty to man."
mklmt10{_}1276{_}And Alice could not choose.
mklmt10{_}1277{_}Too long had she kept her tongue locked with the honour of man.
mklmt10{_}1278{_}"I will tell all my soul about myself," she contended.
mklmt10{_}1279{_}"God knows I am tired of my soul and should like to have it clean and shining once again as when I was a little girl at Kaneohe--"  "But all the corruption of your soul has been with other souls," was Abel Ah Yo's invariable reply.
mklmt10{_}1280{_}"When you have a burden, lay it down.
mklmt10{_}1281{_}You cannot bear a burden and be quit of it at the same time."
mklmt10{_}1282{_}"I will pray to God each day, and many times each day," she urged.
mklmt10{_}1283{_}"I will approach God with humility, with sighs and with tears.
mklmt10{_}1284{_}I will contribute often to the plate, and I will buy Bibles, Bibles, Bibles without end."
mklmt10{_}1285{_}"And God will not smile upon you," God's mouthpiece retorted.
mklmt10{_}1286{_}"And you will remain weary and heavy-laden.
mklmt10{_}1287{_}For you will not have told all your sin, and not until you have told all will you be rid of any."
mklmt10{_}1288{_}"This rebirth is difficult," Alice sighed.
mklmt10{_}1289{_}"Rebirth is even more difficult than birth."
mklmt10{_}1290{_}Abel Ah Yo did anything but comfort her.
mklmt10{_}1291{_}"'Not until you become as a little child .
mklmt10{_}1292{_}.
mklmt10{_}1293{_}. '"
mklmt10{_}1294{_}"If ever I tell my soul, it will be a big telling," she confided.
mklmt10{_}1295{_}"The bigger the reason to tell it then."
mklmt10{_}1296{_}And so the situation remained at deadlock, Abel Ah Yo demanding absolute allegiance to God, and Alice Akana flirting on the fringes of paradise.
mklmt10{_}1297{_}"You bet it will be a big telling, if Alice ever begins," the beach-combing and disreputable kamaainas (old-timers) gleefully told one another over their Palm Tree gin.
mklmt10{_}1298{_}In the clubs the possibility of her telling was of more moment.
mklmt10{_}1299{_}The younger generation of men announced that they had applied for front seats at the telling, while many of the older generation of men joked hollowly about the conversion of Alice.
mklmt10{_}1300{_}Further, Alice found herself abruptly popular with friends who had forgotten her existence for twenty years.
mklmt10{_}1301{_}One afternoon, as Alice, Bible in hand, was taking the electric street car at Hotel and Fort, Cyrus Hodge, sugar factor and magnate, ordered his chauffeur to stop beside her.
mklmt10{_}1302{_}Willy nilly, in excess of friendliness, he had her into his limousine beside him and went three-quarters of an hour out of his way and time personally to conduct her to her destination.
mklmt10{_}1303{_}"Good for sore eyes to see you," he burbled.
mklmt10{_}1304{_}"How the years fly!
mklmt10{_}1305{_}You're looking fine.
mklmt10{_}1306{_}The secret of youth is yours."
mklmt10{_}1307{_}Alice smiled and complimented in return in the royal Polynesian way of friendliness.
mklmt10{_}1308{_}"My, my," Cyrus Hodge reminisced.
mklmt10{_}1309{_}"I was such a boy in those days!"
mklmt10{_}1310{_}"SOME boy," she laughed acquiescence.
mklmt10{_}1311{_}"But knowing no more than the foolishness of a boy in those long- ago days."
mklmt10{_}1312{_}"Remember the night your hack-driver got drunk and left you--"  "S-s-sh!"
mklmt10{_}1313{_}he cautioned.
mklmt10{_}1314{_}"That Jap driver is a high-school graduate and knows more English than either of us.
mklmt10{_}1315{_}Also, I think he is a spy for his Government.
mklmt10{_}1316{_}So why should we tell him anything?
mklmt10{_}1317{_}Besides, I was so very young.
mklmt10{_}1318{_}You remember .
mklmt10{_}1319{_}.
mklmt10{_}1320{_}. "
mklmt10{_}1321{_}"Your cheeks were like the peaches we used to grow before the Mediterranean fruit fly got into them," Alice agreed.
mklmt10{_}1322{_}"I don't think you shaved more than once a week then.
mklmt10{_}1323{_}You were a pretty boy.
mklmt10{_}1324{_}Don't you remember the hula we composed in your honour, the-- "  "S-s-sh!"
mklmt10{_}1325{_}he hushed her.
mklmt10{_}1326{_}"All that's buried and forgotten.
mklmt10{_}1327{_}May it remain forgotten."
mklmt10{_}1328{_}And she was aware that in his eyes was no longer any of the ingenuousness of youth she remembered.
mklmt10{_}1329{_}Instead, his eyes were keen and speculative, searching into her for some assurance that she would not resurrect his particular portion of that buried past.
mklmt10{_}1330{_}"Religion is a good thing for us as we get along into middle age," another old friend told her.
mklmt10{_}1331{_}He was building a magnificent house on Pacific Heights, but had recently married a second time, and was even then on his way to the steamer to welcome home his two daughters just graduated from Vassar.
mklmt10{_}1332{_}"We need religion in our old age, Alice.
mklmt10{_}1333{_}It softens, makes us more tolerant and forgiving of the weaknesses of others--especially the weaknesses of youth of--of others, when they played high and low and didn't know what they were doing."
mklmt10{_}1334{_}He waited anxiously.
mklmt10{_}1335{_}"Yes," she said.
mklmt10{_}1336{_}"We are all born to sin and it is hard to grow out of sin.
mklmt10{_}1337{_}But I grow, I grow."
mklmt10{_}1338{_}"Don't forget, Alice, in those other days I always played square.
mklmt10{_}1339{_}You and I never had a falling out."
mklmt10{_}1340{_}"Not even the night you gave that luau when you were twenty-one and insisted on breaking the glassware after every toast.
mklmt10{_}1341{_}But of course you paid for it."
mklmt10{_}1342{_}"Handsomely," he asserted almost pleadingly.
mklmt10{_}1343{_}"Handsomely," she agreed.
mklmt10{_}1344{_}"I replaced more than double the quantity with what you paid me, so that at the next luau I catered one hundred and twenty plates without having to rent or borrow a dish or glass.
mklmt10{_}1345{_}Lord Mainweather gave that luau--you remember him."
mklmt10{_}1346{_}"I was pig-sticking with him at Mana," the other nodded.
mklmt10{_}1347{_}"We were at a two weeks' house-party there.
mklmt10{_}1348{_}But say, Alice, as you know, I think this religion stuff is all right and better than all right.
mklmt10{_}1349{_}But don't let it carry you off your feet.
mklmt10{_}1350{_}And don't get to telling your soul on me.
mklmt10{_}1351{_}What would my daughters think of that broken glassware!"
mklmt10{_}1352{_}"I always did have an aloha" (warm regard) "for you, Alice," a member of the Senate, fat and bald-headed, assured her.
mklmt10{_}1353{_}And another, a lawyer and a grandfather:  "We were always friends, Alice.
mklmt10{_}1354{_}And remember, any legal advice or handling of business you may require, I'll do for you gladly, and without fees, for the sake of our old-time friendship."
mklmt10{_}1355{_}Came a banker to her late Christmas Eve, with formidable, legal- looking envelopes in his hand which he presented to her.
mklmt10{_}1356{_}"Quite by chance," he explained, "when my people were looking up land-records in Iapio Valley, I found a mortgage of two thousand on your holdings there--that rice land leased to Ah Chin.
mklmt10{_}1357{_}And my mind drifted back to the past when we were all young together, and wild- -a bit wild, to be sure.
mklmt10{_}1358{_}And my heart warmed with the memory of you, and, so, just as an aloha, here's the whole thing cleared off for you."
mklmt10{_}1359{_}Nor was Alice forgotten by her own people.
mklmt10{_}1360{_}Her house became a Mecca for native men and women, usually performing pilgrimage privily after darkness fell, with presents always in their hands-- squid fresh from the reef, opihis and limu, baskets of alligator pears, roasting corn of the earliest from windward Cahu, mangoes and star-apples, taro pink and royal of the finest selection, sucking pigs, banana poi, breadfruit, and crabs caught the very day from Pearl Harbour.
mklmt10{_}1361{_}Mary Mendana, wife of the Portuguese Consul, remembered her with a five-dollar box of candy and a mandarin coat that would have fetched three-quarters of a hundred dollars at a fire sale.
mklmt10{_}1362{_}And Elvira Miyahara Makaena Yin Wap, the wife of Yin Wap the wealthy Chinese importer, brought personally to Alice two entire bolts of pina cloth from the Philippines and a dozen pairs of silk stockings.
mklmt10{_}1363{_}The time passed, and Abel Ah Yo struggled with Alice for a properly penitent heart, and Alice struggled with herself for her soul, while half of Honolulu wickedly or apprehensively hung on the outcome.
mklmt10{_}1364{_}Carnival week was over, polo and the races had come and gone, and the celebration of Fourth of July was ripening, ere Abel Ah Yo beat down by brutal psychology the citadel of her reluctance.
mklmt10{_}1365{_}It was then that he gave his famous exhortation which might be summed up as Abel Ah Yo's definition of eternity.
mklmt10{_}1366{_}Of course, like Billy Sunday on certain occasions, Abel Ah Yo had cribbed the definition.
mklmt10{_}1367{_}But no one in the Islands knew it, and his rating as a revivalist uprose a hundred per cent.
mklmt10{_}1368{_}So successful was his preaching that night, that he reconverted many of his converts, who fell and moaned about the penitent form and crowded for room amongst scores of new converts burnt by the pentecostal fire, including half a company of negro soldiers from the garrisoned Twenty-Fifth Infantry, a dozen troopers from the Fourth Cavalry on its way to the Philippines, as many drunken man- of-war's men, divers ladies from Iwilei, and half the riff-raff of the beach.
mklmt10{_}1369{_}Abel Ah Yo, subtly sympathetic himself by virtue of his racial admixture, knowing human nature like a book and Alice Akana even more so, knew just what he was doing when he arose that memorable night and exposited God, hell, and eternity in terms of Alice Akana's comprehension.
mklmt10{_}1370{_}For, quite by chance, he had discovered her cardinal weakness.
mklmt10{_}1371{_}First of all, like all Polynesians, an ardent lover of nature, he found that earthquake and volcanic eruption were the things of which Alice lived in terror.
mklmt10{_}1372{_}She had been, in the past, on the Big Island, through cataclysms that had slacken grass houses down upon her while she slept, and she had beheld Madame Pele (the Fire or Volcano Goddess) fling red-fluxing lava down the long slopes of Mauna Loa, destroying fish-ponds on the sea-brim and licking up droves of beef cattle, villages, and humans on her fiery way.
mklmt10{_}1373{_}The night before, a slight earthquake had shaken Honolulu and given Alice Akana insomnia.
mklmt10{_}1374{_}And the morning papers had stated that Mauna Kea had broken into eruption, while the lava was rising rapidly in the great pit of Kilauea.
mklmt10{_}1375{_}So, at the meeting, her mind vexed between the terrors of this world and the delights of the eternal world to come, Alice sat down in a front seat in a very definite state of the "jumps."
mklmt10{_}1376{_}And Abel Ah Yo arose and put his finger on the sorest part of her soul.
mklmt10{_}1377{_}Sketching the nature of God in the stereotyped way, but making the stereotyped alive again with his gift of tongues in Pidgin-English and Pidgin-Hawaiian, Abel Ah Yo described the day when the Lord, even His infinite patience at an end, would tell Peter to close his day book and ledgers, command Gabriel to summon all souls to Judgment, and cry out with a voice of thunder: "Welakahao!"
mklmt10{_}1378{_}This anthromorphic deity of Abel Ah Yo thundering the modern Hawaiian-English slang of welakahao at the end of the world, is a fair sample of the revivalist's speech-tools of discourse.
mklmt10{_}1379{_}Welakahao means literally "hot iron."
mklmt10{_}1380{_}It was coined in the Honolulu Iron-works by the hundreds of Hawaiian men there employed, who meant by it "to hustle," "to get a move on," the iron being hot meaning that the time had come to strike.
mklmt10{_}1381{_}"And the Lord cried 'Welakahao,' and the Day of Judgment began and was over wiki-wiki" (quickly) "just like that; for Peter was a better bookkeeper than any on the Waterhouse Trust Company Limited, and, further, Peter's books were true."
mklmt10{_}1382{_}Swiftly Abel Ah Yo divided the sheep from the goats, and hastened the latter down into hell.
mklmt10{_}1383{_}"And now," he demanded, perforce his language on these pages being properly Englished, "what is hell like?
mklmt10{_}1384{_}Oh, my friends, let me describe to you, in a little way, what I have beheld with my own eves on earth of the possibilities of hell.
mklmt10{_}1385{_}I was a young man, a boy, and I was at Hilo.
mklmt10{_}1386{_}Morning began with earthquakes.
mklmt10{_}1387{_}Throughout the day the mighty land continued to shake and tremble, till strong men became seasick, and women clung to trees to escape falling, and cattle were thrown down off their feet.
mklmt10{_}1388{_}I beheld myself a young calf so thrown.
mklmt10{_}1389{_}A night of terror indescribable followed.
mklmt10{_}1390{_}The land was in motion like a canoe in a Kona gale.
mklmt10{_}1391{_}There was an infant crushed to death by its fond mother stepping upon it whilst fleeing her falling house.
mklmt10{_}1392{_}"The heavens were on fire above us.
mklmt10{_}1393{_}We read our Bibles by the light of the heavens, and the print was fine, even for young eyes.
mklmt10{_}1394{_}Those missionary Bibles were always too small of print.
mklmt10{_}1395{_}Forty miles away from us, the heart of hell burst from the lofty mountains and gushed red-blood of fire-melted rock toward the sea.
mklmt10{_}1396{_}With the heavens in vast conflagration and the earth hulaing beneath our feet, was a scene too awful and too majestic to be enjoyed.
mklmt10{_}1397{_}We could think only of the thin bubble-skin of earth between us and the everlasting lake of fire and brimstone, and of God to whom we prayed to save us.
mklmt10{_}1398{_}There were earnest and devout souls who there and then promised their pastors to give not their shaved tithes, but five-tenths of their all to the church, if only the Lord would let them live to contribute.
mklmt10{_}1399{_}"Oh, my friends, God saved us.
mklmt10{_}1400{_}But first he showed us a foretaste of that hell that will yawn for us on the last day, when he cries 'Welakahao!'
mklmt10{_}1401{_}in a voice of thunder.
mklmt10{_}1402{_}When the iron is hot!
mklmt10{_}1403{_}Think of it!
mklmt10{_}1404{_}When the iron is hot for sinners!
mklmt10{_}1405{_}"By the third day, things being much quieter, my friend the preacher and I, being calm in the hand of God, journeyed up Mauna Loa and gazed into the awful pit of Kilauea.
mklmt10{_}1406{_}We gazed down into the fathomless abyss to the lake of fire far below, roaring and dashing its fiery spray into billows and fountaining hundreds of feet into the air like Fourth of July fireworks you have all seen, and all the while we were suffocating and made dizzy by the immense volumes of smoke and brimstone ascending.
mklmt10{_}1407{_}"And I say unto you, no pious person could gaze down upon that scene without recognizing fully the Bible picture of the Pit of Hell.
mklmt10{_}1408{_}Believe me, the writers of the New Testament had nothing on us.
mklmt10{_}1409{_}As for me, my eyes were fixed upon the exhibition before me, and I stood mute and trembling under a sense never before so fully realized of the power, the majesty, and terror of Almighty God--the resources of His wrath, and the untold horrors of the finally impenitent who do not tell their souls and make their peace with the Creator.
mklmt10{_}1410{_}{1}  "But oh, my friends, think you our guides, our native attendants, deep-sunk in heathenism, were affected by such a scene?
mklmt10{_}1411{_}No.
mklmt10{_}1412{_}The devil's hand was upon them.
mklmt10{_}1413{_}Utterly regardless and unimpressed, they were only careful about their supper, chatted about their raw fish, and stretched themselves upon their mats to sleep.
mklmt10{_}1414{_}Children of the devil they were, insensible to the beauties, the sublimities, and the awful terror of God's works.
mklmt10{_}1415{_}But you are not heathen I now address.
mklmt10{_}1416{_}What is a heathen?
mklmt10{_}1417{_}He is one who betrays a stupid insensibility to every elevated idea and to every elevated emotion.
mklmt10{_}1418{_}If you wish to awaken his attention, do not bid him to look down into the Pit of Hell.
mklmt10{_}1419{_}But present him with a calabash of poi, a raw fish, or invite him to some low, grovelling, and sensuous sport.
mklmt10{_}1420{_}Oh, my friends, how lost are they to all that elevates the immortal soul!
mklmt10{_}1421{_}But the preacher and I, sad and sick at heart for them, gazed down into hell.
mklmt10{_}1422{_}Oh, my friends, it WAS hell, the hell of the Scriptures, the hell of eternal torment for the undeserving .
mklmt10{_}1423{_}.
mklmt10{_}1424{_}. "
mklmt10{_}1425{_}Alice Akana was in an ecstasy or hysteria of terror.
mklmt10{_}1426{_}She was mumbling incoherently:  "O Lord, I will give nine-tenths of my all.
mklmt10{_}1427{_}I will give all.
mklmt10{_}1428{_}I will give even the two bolts of pina cloth, the mandarin coat, and the entire dozen silk stockings .
mklmt10{_}1429{_}.
mklmt10{_}1430{_}. "
mklmt10{_}1431{_}By the time she could lend ear again, Abel Ah Yo was launching out on his famous definition of eternity.
mklmt10{_}1432{_}"Eternity is a long time, my friends.
mklmt10{_}1433{_}God lives, and, therefore, God lives inside eternity.
mklmt10{_}1434{_}And God is very old.
mklmt10{_}1435{_}The fires of hell are as old and as everlasting as God.
mklmt10{_}1436{_}How else could there be everlasting torment for those sinners cast down by God into the Pit on the Last Day to burn for ever and for ever through all eternity?
mklmt10{_}1437{_}Oh, my friends, your minds are small--too small to grasp eternity.
mklmt10{_}1438{_}Yet is it given to me, by God's grace, to convey to you an understanding of a tiny bit of eternity.
mklmt10{_}1439{_}"The grains of sand on the beach of Waikiki are as many as the stars, and more.
mklmt10{_}1440{_}No man may count them.
mklmt10{_}1441{_}Did he have a million lives in which to count them, he would have to ask for more time.
mklmt10{_}1442{_}Now let us consider a little, dinky, old minah bird with one broken wing that cannot fly.
mklmt10{_}1443{_}At Waikiki the minah bird that cannot fly takes one grain of sand in its beak and hops, hops, all day lone and for many days, all the day to Pearl Harbour and drops that one grain of sand into the harbour.
mklmt10{_}1444{_}Then it hops, hops, all day and for many days, all the way back to Waikiki for another grain of sand.
mklmt10{_}1445{_}And again it hops, hops all the way back to Pearl Harbour.
mklmt10{_}1446{_}And it continues to do this through the years and centuries, and the thousands and thousands of centuries, until, at last, there remains not one grain of sand at Waikiki and Pearl Harbour is filled up with land and growing coconuts and pine-apples.
mklmt10{_}1447{_}And then, oh my friends, even then, IT WOULD NOT YET BE SUNRISE IN HELL!
mklmt10{_}1448{_}Here, at the smashing impact of so abrupt a climax, unable to withstand the sheer simplicity and objectivity of such artful measurement of a trifle of eternity, Alice Akana's mind broke down and blew up.
mklmt10{_}1449{_}She uprose, reeled blindly, and stumbled to her knees at the penitent form.
mklmt10{_}1450{_}Abel Ah Yo had not finished his preaching, but it was his gift to know crowd psychology, and to feel the heat of the pentecostal conflagration that scorched his audience.
mklmt10{_}1451{_}He called for a rousing revival hymn from his singers, and stepped down to wade among the hallelujah-shouting negro soldiers to Alice Akana.
mklmt10{_}1452{_}And, ere the excitement began to ebb, nine-tenths of his congregation and all his converts were down on knees and praying and shouting aloud an immensity of contriteness and sin.
mklmt10{_}1453{_}Word came, via telephone, almost simultaneously to the Pacific and University Clubs, that at last Alice was telling her soul in meeting; and, by private machine and taxi-cab, for the first time Abel Ah Yo's revival was invaded by those of caste and place.
mklmt10{_}1454{_}The first comers beheld the curious sight of Hawaiian, Chinese, and all variegated racial mixtures of the smelting-pot of Hawaii, men and women, fading out and slinking away through the exits of Abel Ah Yo's tabernacle.
mklmt10{_}1455{_}But those who were sneaking out were mostly men, while those who remained were avid-faced as they hung on Alice's utterance.
mklmt10{_}1456{_}Never was a more fearful and damning community narrative enunciated in the entire Pacific, north and south, than that enunciated by Alice Akana; the penitent Phryne of Honolulu.
mklmt10{_}1457{_}"Huh!"
mklmt10{_}1458{_}the first comers heard her saying, having already disposed of most of the venial sins of the lesser ones of her memory.
mklmt10{_}1459{_}"You think this man, Stephen Makekau, is the son of Moses Makekau and Minnie Ah Ling, and has a legal right to the two hundred and eight dollars he draws down each month from Parke Richards Limited, for the lease of the fish-pond to Bill Kong at Amana.
mklmt10{_}1460{_}Not so.
mklmt10{_}1461{_}Stephen Makekau is not the son of Moses.
mklmt10{_}1462{_}He is the son of Aaron Kama and Tillie Naone.
mklmt10{_}1463{_}He was given as a present, as a feeding child, to Moses and Minnie, by Aaron and Tillie.
mklmt10{_}1464{_}I know.
mklmt10{_}1465{_}Moses and Minnie and Aaron and Tillie are dead.
mklmt10{_}1466{_}Yet I know and can prove it.
mklmt10{_}1467{_}Old Mrs. Poepoe is still alive.
mklmt10{_}1468{_}I was present when Stephen was born, and in the night-time, when he was two months old, I myself carried him as a present to Moses and Minnie, and old Mrs. Poepoe carried the lantern.
mklmt10{_}1469{_}This secret has been one of my sins.
mklmt10{_}1470{_}It has kept me from God.
mklmt10{_}1471{_}Now I am free of it.
mklmt10{_}1472{_}Young Archie Makekau, who collects bills for the Gas Company and plays baseball in the afternoons, and drinks too much gin, should get that two hundred and eight dollars the first of each month from Parke Richards Limited.
mklmt10{_}1473{_}He will blow it in on gin and a Ford automobile.
mklmt10{_}1474{_}Stephen is a good man.
mklmt10{_}1475{_}Archie is no good.
mklmt10{_}1476{_}Also he is a liar, and he has served two sentences on the reef, and was in reform school before that.
mklmt10{_}1477{_}Yet God demands the truth, and Archie will get the money and make a bad use of it."
mklmt10{_}1478{_}And in such fashion Alice rambled on through the experiences of her long and full-packed life.
mklmt10{_}1479{_}And women forgot they were in the tabernacle, and men too, and faces darkened with passion as they learned for the first time the long-buried secrets of their other halves.
mklmt10{_}1480{_}"The lawyers' offices will be crowded to-morrow morning," MacIlwaine, chief of detectives, paused long enough from storing away useful information to lean and mutter in Colonel Stilton's ear.
mklmt10{_}1481{_}Colonel Stilton grinned affirmation, although the chief of detectives could not fail to note the ghastliness of the grin.
mklmt10{_}1482{_}"There is a banker in Honolulu.
mklmt10{_}1483{_}You all know his name.
mklmt10{_}1484{_}He is 'way up, swell society because of his wife.
mklmt10{_}1485{_}He owns much stock in General Plantations and Inter-Island."
mklmt10{_}1486{_}MacIlwaine recognized the growing portrait and forbore to chuckle.
mklmt10{_}1487{_}"His name is Colonel Stilton.
mklmt10{_}1488{_}Last Christmas Eve he came to my house with big aloha" (love) "and gave me mortgages on my land in Iapio Valley, all cancelled, for two thousand dollars' worth.
mklmt10{_}1489{_}Now why did he have such big cash aloha for me?
mklmt10{_}1490{_}I will tell you .
mklmt10{_}1491{_}.
mklmt10{_}1492{_}. "
mklmt10{_}1493{_}And tell she did, throwing the searchlight on ancient business transactions and political deals which from their inception had lurked in the dark.
mklmt10{_}1494{_}"This," Alice concluded the episode, "has long been a sin upon my conscience, and kept my heart from God.
mklmt10{_}1495{_}"And Harold Miles was that time President of the Senate, and next week he bought three town lots at Pearl Harbour, and painted his Honolulu house, and paid up his back dues in his clubs.
mklmt10{_}1496{_}Also the Ramsay home at Honokiki was left by will to the people if the Government would keep it up.
mklmt10{_}1497{_}But if the Government, after two years, did not begin to keep it up, then would it go to the Ramsay heirs, whom old Ramsay hated like poison.
mklmt10{_}1498{_}Well, it went to the heirs all right.
mklmt10{_}1499{_}Their lawyer was Charley Middleton, and he had me help fix it with the Government men.
mklmt10{_}1500{_}And their names were .
mklmt10{_}1501{_}.
mklmt10{_}1502{_}. "
mklmt10{_}1503{_}Six names, from both branches of the Legislature, Alice recited, and added:  "Maybe they all painted their houses after that.
mklmt10{_}1504{_}For the first time have I spoken.
mklmt10{_}1505{_}My heart is much lighter and softer.
mklmt10{_}1506{_}It has been coated with an armour of house-paint against the Lord.
mklmt10{_}1507{_}And there is Harry Werther.
mklmt10{_}1508{_}He was in the Senate that time.
mklmt10{_}1509{_}Everybody said bad things about him, and he was never re-elected.
mklmt10{_}1510{_}Yet his house was not painted.
mklmt10{_}1511{_}He was honest.
mklmt10{_}1512{_}To this day his house is not painted, as everybody knows.
mklmt10{_}1513{_}"There is Jim Lokendamper.
mklmt10{_}1514{_}He has a bad heart.
mklmt10{_}1515{_}I heard him, only last week, right here before you all, tell his soul.
mklmt10{_}1516{_}He did not tell all his soul, and he lied to God.
mklmt10{_}1517{_}I am not lying to God.
mklmt10{_}1518{_}It is a big telling, but I am telling everything.
mklmt10{_}1519{_}Now Azalea Akau, sitting right over there, is his wife.
mklmt10{_}1520{_}But Lizzie Lokendamper is his married wife.
mklmt10{_}1521{_}A long time ago he had the great aloha for Azalea.
mklmt10{_}1522{_}You think her uncle, who went to California and died, left her by will that two thousand five hundred dollars she got.
mklmt10{_}1523{_}Her uncle did not.
mklmt10{_}1524{_}I know.
mklmt10{_}1525{_}Her uncle cried broke in California, and Jim Lokendamper sent eighty dollars to California to bury him.
mklmt10{_}1526{_}Jim Lokendamper had a piece of land in Kohala he got from his mother's aunt.
mklmt10{_}1527{_}Lizzie, his married wife, did not know this.
mklmt10{_}1528{_}So he sold it to the Kohala Ditch Company and wave the twenty-five hundred to Azalea Akau--"  Here, Lizzie, the married wife, upstood like a fury long-thwarted, and, in lieu of her husband, already fled, flung herself tooth and nail on Azalea.
mklmt10{_}1529{_}"Wait, Lizzie Lokendamper!"
mklmt10{_}1530{_}Alice cried out.
mklmt10{_}1531{_}"I have much weight of you on my heart and some house-paint too .
mklmt10{_}1532{_}.
mklmt10{_}1533{_}. "
mklmt10{_}1534{_}And when she had finished her disclosure of how Lizzie had painted her house, Azalea was up and raging.
mklmt10{_}1535{_}"Wait, Azalea Akau.
mklmt10{_}1536{_}I shall now lighten my heart about you.
mklmt10{_}1537{_}And it is not house-paint.
mklmt10{_}1538{_}Jim always paid that.
mklmt10{_}1539{_}It is your new bath- tub and modern plumbing that is heavy on me .
mklmt10{_}1540{_}.
mklmt10{_}1541{_}. "
mklmt10{_}1542{_}Worse, much worse, about many and sundry, did Alice Akana have to say, cutting high in business, financial, and social life, as well as low.
mklmt10{_}1543{_}None was too high nor too low to escape; and not until two in the morning, before an entranced audience that packed the tabernacle to the doors, did she complete her recital of the personal and detailed iniquities she knew of the community in which she had lived intimately all her days.
mklmt10{_}1544{_}Just as she was finishing, she remembered more.
mklmt10{_}1545{_}"Huh!"
mklmt10{_}1546{_}she sniffed.
mklmt10{_}1547{_}"I gave last week one lot worth eight hundred dollars cash market price to Abel Ah Yo to pay running expenses and add up in Peter's books in heaven.
mklmt10{_}1548{_}Where did I get that lot?
mklmt10{_}1549{_}You all think Mr. Fleming Jason is a good man.
mklmt10{_}1550{_}He is more crooked than the entrance was to Pearl Lochs before the United States Government straightened the channel.
mklmt10{_}1551{_}He has liver disease now; but his sickness is a judgment of God, and he will die crooked.
mklmt10{_}1552{_}Mr. Fleming Jason gave me that lot twenty-two years ago, when its cash market price was thirty-five dollars.
mklmt10{_}1553{_}Because his aloha for me was big?
mklmt10{_}1554{_}No.
mklmt10{_}1555{_}He never had aloha inside of him except for dollars.
mklmt10{_}1556{_}"You listen.
mklmt10{_}1557{_}Mr. Fleming Jason put a great sin upon me.
mklmt10{_}1558{_}When Frank Lomiloli was at my house, full of gin, for which gin Mr. Fleming Jason paid me in advance five times over, I got Frank Lomiloli to sign his name to the sale paper of his town land for one hundred dollars.
mklmt10{_}1559{_}It was worth six hundred then.
mklmt10{_}1560{_}It is worth twenty thousand now.
mklmt10{_}1561{_}Maybe you want to know where that town land is.
mklmt10{_}1562{_}I will tell you and remove it off my heart.
mklmt10{_}1563{_}It is on King Street, where is now the Come Again Saloon, the Japanese Taxicab Company garage, the Smith & Wilson plumbing shop, and the Ambrosia lee Cream Parlours, with the two more stories big Addison Lodging House overhead.
mklmt10{_}1564{_}And it is all wood, and always has been well painted.
mklmt10{_}1565{_}Yesterday they started painting it attain.
mklmt10{_}1566{_}But that paint will not stand between me and God.
mklmt10{_}1567{_}There are no more paint pots between me and my path to heaven."
mklmt10{_}1568{_}The morning and evening papers of the day following held an unholy hush on the greatest news story of years; but Honolulu was half a- giggle and half aghast at the whispered reports, not always basely exaggerated, that circulated wherever two Honoluluans chanced to meet.
mklmt10{_}1569{_}"Our mistake," said Colonel Chilton, at the club, "was that we did not, at the very first, appoint a committee of safety to keep track of Alice's soul."
