mklmt10{_}2295{_}His gods were the sea and fish gods, and he was born with knowledge of the language of fishes, which the fishes did not know until the sharks found it out one day when they heard him talk it.
mklmt10{_}2296{_}"It happened this way.
mklmt10{_}2297{_}The word had been brought, and the commands, by swift runners, that the king was making a progress around the island, and that on the next day a luau" (feast) "was to be served him by the dwellers here of Waihee.
mklmt10{_}2298{_}It was always a hardship, when the king made a progress, for the few dwellers in small places to fill his many stomachs with food.
mklmt10{_}2299{_}For he came always with his wife and her women, with his priests and sorcerers, his dancers and flute-players, and hula-singers, and fighting men and servants, and his high chiefs with their wives, and sorcerers, and fighting men, and servants.
mklmt10{_}2300{_}"Sometimes, in small places like Waihee, the path of his journey was marked afterward by leanness and famine.
mklmt10{_}2301{_}But a king must be fed, and it is not good to anger a king.
mklmt10{_}2302{_}So, like warning in advance of disaster, Waihee heard of his coming, and all food- getters of field and pond and mountain and sea were busied with getting food for the feast.
mklmt10{_}2303{_}And behold, everything was got, from the choicest of royal taro to sugar-cane joints for the roasting, from opihis to limu, from fowl to wild pig and poi-fed puppies-- everything save one thing.
mklmt10{_}2304{_}The fishermen failed to get lobsters.
mklmt10{_}2305{_}"Now be it known that the king's favourite food was lobster.
mklmt10{_}2306{_}He esteemed it above all kai-kai" (food), "and his runners had made special mention of it.
mklmt10{_}2307{_}And there were no lobsters, and it is not good to anger a king in the belly of him.
mklmt10{_}2308{_}Too many sharks had come inside the reef.
mklmt10{_}2309{_}That was the trouble.
mklmt10{_}2310{_}A young girl and an old man had been eaten by them.
mklmt10{_}2311{_}And of the young men who dared dive for lobsters, one was eaten, and one lost an arm, and another lost one hand and one foot.
mklmt10{_}2312{_}"But there was Keikiwai, the Water Baby, only eleven years old, but half fish himself and talking the language of fishes.
mklmt10{_}2313{_}To his father the head men came, begging him to send the Water Baby to get lobsters to fill the king's belly and divert his anger.
mklmt10{_}2314{_}"Now this what happened was known and observed.
mklmt10{_}2315{_}For the fishermen, and their women, and the taro-growers and the bird-catchers, and the head men, and all Waihee, came down and stood back from the edge of the rock where the Water Baby stood and looked down at the lobsters far beneath on the bottom.
mklmt10{_}2316{_}"And a shark, looking up with its cat's eyes, observed him, and sent out the shark-call of 'fresh meat' to assemble all the sharks in the lagoon.
mklmt10{_}2317{_}For the sharks work thus together, which is why they are strong.
mklmt10{_}2318{_}And the sharks answered the call till there were forty of them, long ones and short ones and lean ones and round ones, forty of them by count; and they talked to one another, saying:  'Look at that titbit of a child, that morsel delicious of human-flesh sweetness without the salt of the sea in it, of which salt we have too much, savoury and good to eat, melting to delight under our hearts as our bellies embrace it and extract from it its sweet.'
mklmt10{_}2319{_}"Much more they said, saying:  'He has come for the lobsters.
mklmt10{_}2320{_}When he dives in he is for one of us.
mklmt10{_}2321{_}Not like the old man we ate yesterday, tough to dryness with age, nor like the young men whose members were too hard-muscled, but tender, so tender that he will melt in our gullets ere our bellies receive him.
mklmt10{_}2322{_}When he dives in, we will all rush for him, and the lucky one of us will get him, and, gulp, he will be gone, one bite and one swallow, into the belly of the luckiest one of us.'
mklmt10{_}2323{_}"And Keikiwai, the Water Baby, heard the conspiracy, knowing the shark language; and he addressed a prayer, in the shark language, to the shark god Moku-halii, and the sharks heard and waved their tails to one another and winked their cat's eyes in token that they understood his talk.
mklmt10{_}2324{_}And then he said:  'I shall now dive for a lobster for the king.
mklmt10{_}2325{_}And no hurt shall befall me, because the shark with the shortest tail is my friend and will protect me.
mklmt10{_}2326{_}"And, so saying, he picked up a chunk of lava-rock and tossed it into the water, with a big splash, twenty feet to one side.
mklmt10{_}2327{_}The forty sharks rushed for the splash, while he dived, and by the time they discovered they had missed him, he had gone to bottom and come back and climbed out, within his hand a fat lobster, a wahine lobster, full of eggs, for the king.
mklmt10{_}2328{_}"'Ha!'
mklmt10{_}2329{_}said the sharks, very angry.
mklmt10{_}2330{_}'There is among us a traitor.
mklmt10{_}2331{_}The titbit of a child, the morsel of sweetness, has spoken, and has exposed the one among us who has saved him.
mklmt10{_}2332{_}Let us now measure the lengths of our tails!
mklmt10{_}2333{_}"Which they did, in a long row, side by side, the shorter-tailed ones cheating and stretching to gain length on themselves, the longer-tailed ones cheating and stretching in order not to be out- cheated and out-stretched.
mklmt10{_}2334{_}They were very angry with the one with the shortest tail, and him they rushed upon from every side and devoured till nothing was left of him.
mklmt10{_}2335{_}"Again they listened while they waited for the Water Baby to dive in.
mklmt10{_}2336{_}And again the Water Baby made his prayer in the shark language to Moku-halii, and said:  'The shark with the shortest tail is my friend and will protect me.'
mklmt10{_}2337{_}And again the Water Baby tossed in a chunk of lava, this time twenty feet away off to the other side.
mklmt10{_}2338{_}The sharks rushed for the splash, and in their haste ran into one another, and splashed with their tails till the water was all foam, and they could see nothing, each thinking some other was swallowing the titbit.
mklmt10{_}2339{_}And the Water Baby came up and climbed out with another fat lobster for the king.
mklmt10{_}2340{_}"And the thirty-nine sharks measured tails, devoting the one with the shortest tail, so that there were only thirty-eight sharks.
mklmt10{_}2341{_}And the Water Baby continued to do what I have said, and the sharks to do what I have told you, while for each shark that was eaten by his brothers there was another fat lobster laid on the rock for the king.
mklmt10{_}2342{_}Of course, there was much quarrelling and argument among the sharks when it came to measuring tails; but in the end it worked out in rightness and justice, for, when only two sharks were left, they were the two biggest of the original forty.
mklmt10{_}2343{_}"And the Water Baby again claimed the shark with the shortest tail was his friend, fooled the two sharks with another lava-chunk, and brought up another lobster.
mklmt10{_}2344{_}The two sharks each claimed the other had the shorter tail, and each fought to eat the other, and the one with the longer tail won--"  "Hold, O Kohokumu!"
mklmt10{_}2345{_}I interrupted.
mklmt10{_}2346{_}"Remember that that shark had already--"  "I know just what you are going to say," he snatched his recital back from me.
mklmt10{_}2347{_}"And you are right.
mklmt10{_}2348{_}It took him so long to eat the thirty-ninth shark, for inside the thirty-ninth shark were already the nineteen other sharks he had eaten, and inside the fortieth shark were already the nineteen other sharks he had eaten, and he did not have the appetite he had started with.
mklmt10{_}2349{_}But do not forget he was a very big shark to begin with.
mklmt10{_}2350{_}"It took him so long to eat the other shark, and the nineteen sharks inside the other shark, that he was still eating when darkness fell, and the people of Waihee went away home with all the lobsters for the king.
mklmt10{_}2351{_}And didn't they find the last shark on the beach next morning dead, and burst wide open with all he had eaten?"
mklmt10{_}2352{_}Kohokumu fetched a full stop and held my eyes with his own shrewd ones.
mklmt10{_}2353{_}"Hold, O Lakana!"
mklmt10{_}2354{_}he checked the speech that rushed to my tongue.
mklmt10{_}2355{_}"I know what next you would say.
mklmt10{_}2356{_}You would say that with my own eyes I did not see this, and therefore that I do not know what I have been telling you.
mklmt10{_}2357{_}But I do know, and I can prove it.
mklmt10{_}2358{_}My father's father knew the grandson of the Water Baby's father's uncle.
mklmt10{_}2359{_}Also, there, on the rocky point to which I point my finger now, is where the Water Baby stood and dived.
mklmt10{_}2360{_}I have dived for lobsters there myself.
mklmt10{_}2361{_}It is a great place for lobsters.
mklmt10{_}2362{_}Also, and often, have I seen sharks there.
mklmt10{_}2363{_}And there, on the bottom, as I should know, for I have seen and counted them, are the thirty- nine lava-rocks thrown in by the Water Baby as I have described."
mklmt10{_}2364{_}"But--" I began.
mklmt10{_}2365{_}"Ha!"
mklmt10{_}2366{_}he baffled me.
mklmt10{_}2367{_}"Look!
mklmt10{_}2368{_}While we have talked the fish have begun again to bite."
mklmt10{_}2369{_}He pointed to three of the bamboo poles erect and devil-dancing in token that fish were hooked and struggling on the lines beneath.
mklmt10{_}2370{_}As he bent to his paddle, he muttered, for my benefit:  "Of course I know.
mklmt10{_}2371{_}The thirty-nine lava rocks are still there.
mklmt10{_}2372{_}You can count them any day for yourself.
mklmt10{_}2373{_}Of course I know, and I know for a fact."
mklmt10{_}2374{_}GLEN ELLEN.
mklmt10{_}2375{_}October 2, 1916.
mklmt10{_}2376{_}THE TEARS OF AH KIM    There was a great noise and racket, but no scandal, in Honolulu's Chinatown.
mklmt10{_}2377{_}Those within hearing distance merely shrugged their shoulders and smiled tolerantly at the disturbance as an affair of accustomed usualness.
mklmt10{_}2378{_}"What is it?"
mklmt10{_}2379{_}asked Chin Mo, down with a sharp pleurisy, of his wife, who had paused for a second at the open window to listen.
mklmt10{_}2380{_}"Only Ah Kim," was her reply.
mklmt10{_}2381{_}"His mother is beating him again."
mklmt10{_}2382{_}The fracas was taking place in the garden, behind the living rooms that were at the back of the store that fronted on the street with the proud sign above:  AH KIM COMPANY, GENERAL MERCHANDISE.
mklmt10{_}2383{_}The garden was a miniature domain, twenty feet square, that somehow cunningly seduced the eye into a sense and seeming of illimitable vastness.
mklmt10{_}2384{_}There were forests of dwarf pines and oaks, centuries old yet two or three feet in height, and imported at enormous care and expense.
mklmt10{_}2385{_}A tiny bridge, a pace across, arched over a miniature river that flowed with rapids and cataracts from a miniature lake stocked with myriad-finned, orange-miracled goldfish that in proportion to the lake and landscape were whales.
mklmt10{_}2386{_}On every side the many windows of the several-storied shack-buildings looked down.
mklmt10{_}2387{_}In the centre of the garden, on the narrow gravelled walk close beside the lake Ah Kim was noisily receiving his beating.
mklmt10{_}2388{_}No Chinese lad of tender and beatable years was Ah Kim.
mklmt10{_}2389{_}His was the store of Ah Kim Company, and his was the achievement of building it up through the long years from the shoestring of savings of a contract coolie labourer to a bank account in four figures and a credit that was gilt edged.
mklmt10{_}2390{_}An even half-century of summers and winters had passed over his head, and, in the passing, fattened him comfortably and snugly.
mklmt10{_}2391{_}Short of stature, his full front was as rotund as a water-melon seed.
mklmt10{_}2392{_}His face was moon- faced.
mklmt10{_}2393{_}His garb was dignified and silken, and his black-silk skull-cap with the red button atop, now, alas!
mklmt10{_}2394{_}fallen on the ground, was the skull-cap worn by the successful and dignified merchants of his race.
mklmt10{_}2395{_}But his appearance, in this moment of the present, was anything but dignified.
mklmt10{_}2396{_}Dodging and ducking under a rain of blows from a bamboo cane, he was crouched over in a half-doubled posture.
mklmt10{_}2397{_}When he was rapped on the knuckles and elbows, with which he shielded his face and head, his winces were genuine and involuntary.
mklmt10{_}2398{_}From the many surrounding windows the neighbourhood looked down with placid enjoyment.
mklmt10{_}2399{_}And she who wielded the stick so shrewdly from long practice!
mklmt10{_}2400{_}Seventy-four years old, she looked every minute of her time.
mklmt10{_}2401{_}Her thin legs were encased in straight-lined pants of linen stiff- textured and shiny-black.
mklmt10{_}2402{_}Her scraggly grey hair was drawn unrelentingly and flatly back from a narrow, unrelenting forehead.
mklmt10{_}2403{_}Eyebrows she had none, having long since shed them.
mklmt10{_}2404{_}Her eyes, of pin-hole tininess, were blackest black.
mklmt10{_}2405{_}She was shockingly cadaverous.
mklmt10{_}2406{_}Her shrivelled forearm, exposed by the loose sleeve, possessed no more of muscle than several taut bowstrings stretched across meagre bone under yellow, parchment-like skin.
mklmt10{_}2407{_}Along this mummy arm jade bracelets shot up and down and clashed with every blow.
mklmt10{_}2408{_}"Ah!"
mklmt10{_}2409{_}she cried out, rhythmically accenting her blows in series of three to each shrill observation.
mklmt10{_}2410{_}"I forbade you to talk to Li Faa.
mklmt10{_}2411{_}To-day you stopped on the street with her.
mklmt10{_}2412{_}Not an hour ago.
mklmt10{_}2413{_}Half an hour by the clock you talked.--What is that?"
mklmt10{_}2414{_}"It was the thrice-accursed telephone," Ah Kim muttered, while she suspended the stick to catch what he said.
mklmt10{_}2415{_}"Mrs. Chang Lucy told you.
mklmt10{_}2416{_}I know she did.
mklmt10{_}2417{_}I saw her see me.
mklmt10{_}2418{_}I shall have the telephone taken out.
mklmt10{_}2419{_}It is of the devil."
mklmt10{_}2420{_}"It is a device of all the devils," Mrs. Tai Fu agreed, taking a fresh grip on the stick.
mklmt10{_}2421{_}"Yet shall the telephone remain.
mklmt10{_}2422{_}I like to talk with Mrs. Chang Lucy over the telephone."
mklmt10{_}2423{_}"She has the eyes of ten thousand cats," quoth Ah Kim, ducking and receiving the stick stinging on his knuckles.
mklmt10{_}2424{_}"And the tongues of ten thousand toads," he supplemented ere his next duck.
mklmt10{_}2425{_}"She is an impudent-faced and evil-mannered hussy," Mrs. Tai Fu accented.
mklmt10{_}2426{_}"Mrs. Chang Lucy was ever that," Ah Kim murmured like the dutiful son he was.
mklmt10{_}2427{_}"I speak of Li Faa," his mother corrected with stick emphasis.
mklmt10{_}2428{_}"She is only half Chinese, as you know.
mklmt10{_}2429{_}Her mother was a shameless kanaka.
mklmt10{_}2430{_}She wears skirts like the degraded haole women--also corsets, as I have seen for myself.
mklmt10{_}2431{_}Where are her children?
mklmt10{_}2432{_}Yet has she buried two husbands."
mklmt10{_}2433{_}"The one was drowned, the other kicked by a horse," Ah Kim qualified.
mklmt10{_}2434{_}"A year of her, unworthy son of a noble father, and you would gladly be going out to get drowned or be kicked by a horse."
mklmt10{_}2435{_}Subdued chucklings and laughter from the window audience applauded her point.
mklmt10{_}2436{_}"You buried two husbands yourself, revered mother," Ah Kim was stung to retort.
mklmt10{_}2437{_}"I had the good taste not to marry a third.
mklmt10{_}2438{_}Besides, my two husbands died honourably in their beds.
mklmt10{_}2439{_}They were not kicked by horses nor drowned at sea.
mklmt10{_}2440{_}What business is it of our neighbours that you should inform them I have had two husbands, or ten, or none?
mklmt10{_}2441{_}You have made a scandal of me, before all our neighbours, and for that I shall now give you a real beating."
mklmt10{_}2442{_}Ah Kim endured the staccato rain of blows, and said when his mother paused, breathless and weary:  "Always have I insisted and pleaded, honourable mother, that you beat me in the house, with the windows and doors closed tight, and not in the open street or the garden open behind the house.
mklmt10{_}2443{_}"You have called this unthinkable Li Faa the Silvery Moon Blossom," Mrs. Tai Fu rejoined, quite illogically and femininely, but with utmost success in so far as she deflected her son from continuance of the thrust he had so swiftly driven home.
mklmt10{_}2444{_}"Mrs. Chang Lucy told you," he charged.
mklmt10{_}2445{_}"I was told over the telephone," his mother evaded.
mklmt10{_}2446{_}"I do not know all voices that speak to me over that contrivance of all the devils."
mklmt10{_}2447{_}Strangely, Ah Kim made no effort to run away from his mother, which he could easily have done.
mklmt10{_}2448{_}She, on the other hand, found fresh cause for more stick blows.
mklmt10{_}2449{_}"Ah!
mklmt10{_}2450{_}Stubborn one!
mklmt10{_}2451{_}Why do you not cry?
mklmt10{_}2452{_}Mule that shameth its ancestors!
mklmt10{_}2453{_}Never have I made you cry.
mklmt10{_}2454{_}From the time you were a little boy I have never made you cry.
mklmt10{_}2455{_}Answer me!
mklmt10{_}2456{_}Why do you not cry?"
mklmt10{_}2457{_}Weak and breathless from her exertions, she dropped the stick and panted and shook as if with a nervous palsy.
mklmt10{_}2458{_}"I do not know, except that it is my way," Ah Kim replied, gazing solicitously at his mother.
mklmt10{_}2459{_}"I shall bring you a chair now, and you will sit down and rest and feel better."
mklmt10{_}2460{_}But she flung away from him with a snort and tottered agedly across the garden into the house.
mklmt10{_}2461{_}Meanwhile recovering his skull-cap and smoothing his disordered attire, Ah Kim rubbed his hurts and gazed after her with eyes of devotion.
mklmt10{_}2462{_}He even smiled, and almost might it appear that he had enjoyed the beating.
mklmt10{_}2463{_}Ah Kim had been so beaten ever since he was a boy, when he lived on the high banks of the eleventh cataract of the Yangtse river.
mklmt10{_}2464{_}Here his father had been born and toiled all his days from young manhood as a towing coolie.
mklmt10{_}2465{_}When he died, Ah Kim, in his own young manhood, took up the same honourable profession.
mklmt10{_}2466{_}Farther back than all remembered annals of the family, had the males of it been towing coolies.
mklmt10{_}2467{_}At the time of Christ his direct ancestors had been doing the same thing, meeting the precisely similarly modelled junks below the white water at the foot of the canyon, bending the half-mile of rope to each junk, and, according to size, tailing on from a hundred to two hundred coolies of them and by sheer, two- legged man-power, bowed forward and down till their hands touched the ground and their faces were sometimes within a foot of it, dragging the junk up through the white water to the head of the canyon.
mklmt10{_}2468{_}Apparently, down all the intervening centuries, the payment of the trade had not picked up.
mklmt10{_}2469{_}His father, his father's father, and himself, Ah Kim, had received the same invariable remuneration--per junk one-fourteenth of a cent, at the rate he had since learned money was valued in Hawaii.
mklmt10{_}2470{_}On long lucky summer days when the waters were easy, the junks many, the hours of daylight sixteen, sixteen hours of such heroic toil would earn over a cent.
mklmt10{_}2471{_}But in a whole year a towing coolie did not earn more than a dollar and a half.
mklmt10{_}2472{_}People could and did live on such an income.
mklmt10{_}2473{_}There were women servants who received a yearly wage of a dollar.
mklmt10{_}2474{_}The net- makers of Ti Wi earned between a dollar and two dollars a year.
mklmt10{_}2475{_}They lived on such wages, or, at least, they did not die on them.
mklmt10{_}2476{_}But for the towing coolies there were pickings, which were what made the profession honourable and the guild a close and hereditary corporation or labour union.
mklmt10{_}2477{_}One junk in five that was dragged up through the rapids or lowered down was wrecked.
mklmt10{_}2478{_}One junk in every ten was a total loss.
mklmt10{_}2479{_}The coolies of the towing guild knew the freaks and whims of the currents, and grappled, and raked, and netted a wet harvest from the river.
mklmt10{_}2480{_}They of the guild were looked up to by lesser coolies, for they could afford to drink brick tea and eat number four rice every day.
mklmt10{_}2481{_}And Ah Kim had been contented and proud, until, one bitter spring day of driving sleet and hail, he dragged ashore a drowning Cantonese sailor.
mklmt10{_}2482{_}It was this wanderer, thawing out by his fire, who first named the magic name Hawaii to him.
mklmt10{_}2483{_}He had himself never been to that labourer's paradise, said the sailor; but many Chinese had gone there from Canton, and he had heard the talk of their letters written back.
mklmt10{_}2484{_}In Hawaii was never frost nor famine.
mklmt10{_}2485{_}The very pigs, never fed, were ever fat of the generous offal disdained by man.
mklmt10{_}2486{_}A Cantonese or Yangtse family could live on the waste of an Hawaii coolie.
mklmt10{_}2487{_}And wages!
mklmt10{_}2488{_}In gold dollars, ten a month, or, in trade dollars, two a month, was what the contract Chinese coolie received from the white-devil sugar kings.
mklmt10{_}2489{_}In a year the coolie received the prodigious sum of two hundred and forty trade dollars- -more than a hundred times what a coolie, toiling ten times as hard, received on the eleventh cataract of the Yangtse.
mklmt10{_}2490{_}In short, all things considered, an Hawaii coolie was one hundred times better off, and, when the amount of labour was estimated, a thousand times better off.
mklmt10{_}2491{_}In addition was the wonderful climate.
mklmt10{_}2492{_}When Ah Kim was twenty-four, despite his mother's pleadings and beatings, he resigned from the ancient and honourable guild of the eleventh cataract towing coolies, left his mother to go into a boss coolie's household as a servant for a dollar a year, and an annual dress to cost not less than thirty cents, and himself departed down the Yangtse to the great sea.
mklmt10{_}2493{_}Many were his adventures and severe his toils and hardships ere, as a salt-sea junk-sailor, he won to Canton.
mklmt10{_}2494{_}When he was twenty-six he signed five years of his life and labour away to the Hawaii sugar kings and departed, one of eight hundred contract coolies, for that far island land, on a festering steamer run by a crazy captain and drunken officers and rejected of Lloyds.
mklmt10{_}2495{_}Honourable, among labourers, had Ah Kim's rating been as a towing coolie.
mklmt10{_}2496{_}In Hawaii, receiving a hundred times more pay, he found himself looked down upon as the lowest of the low--a plantation coolie, than which could be nothing lower.
mklmt10{_}2497{_}But a coolie whose ancestors had towed junks up the eleventh cataract of the Yangtse since before the birth of Christ inevitably inherits one character in large degree, namely, the character of patience.
mklmt10{_}2498{_}This patience was Ah Kim's.
mklmt10{_}2499{_}At the end of five years, his compulsory servitude over, thin as ever in body, in bank account he lacked just ten trade dollars of possessing a thousand trade dollars.
mklmt10{_}2500{_}On this sum he could have gone back to the Yangtse and retired for life a really wealthy man.
mklmt10{_}2501{_}He would have possessed a larger sum, had he not, on occasion, conservatively played che fa and fan tan, and had he not, for a twelve-month, toiled among the centipedes and scorpions of the stifling cane-fields in the semi-dream of a continuous opium debauch.
mklmt10{_}2502{_}Why he had not toiled the whole five years under the spell of opium was the expensiveness of the habit.
mklmt10{_}2503{_}He had had no moral scruples.
mklmt10{_}2504{_}The drug had cost too much.
mklmt10{_}2505{_}But Ah Kim did not return to China.
mklmt10{_}2506{_}He had observed the business life of Hawaii and developed a vaulting ambition.
mklmt10{_}2507{_}For six months, in order to learn business and English at the bottom, he clerked in the plantation store.
mklmt10{_}2508{_}At the end of this time he knew more about that particular store than did ever plantation manager know about any plantation store.
mklmt10{_}2509{_}When he resigned his position he was receiving forty gold a month, or eighty trade, and he was beginning to put on flesh.
mklmt10{_}2510{_}Also, his attitude toward mere contract coolies had become distinctively aristocratic.
mklmt10{_}2511{_}The manager offered to raise him to sixty fold, which, by the year, would constitute a fabulous fourteen hundred and forty trade, or seven hundred times his annual earning on the Yangtse as a two-legged horse at one- fourteenth of a gold cent per junk.
mklmt10{_}2512{_}Instead of accepting, Ah Kim departed to Honolulu, and in the big general merchandise store of Fong & Chow Fong began at the bottom for fifteen gold per month.
mklmt10{_}2513{_}He worked a year and a half, and resigned when he was thirty-three, despite the seventy-five gold per month his Chinese employers were paying him.
mklmt10{_}2514{_}Then it was that he put up his own sign:  AH KIM COMPANY, GENERAL MERCHANDISE.
mklmt10{_}2515{_}Also, better fed, there was about his less meagre figure a foreshadowing of the melon-seed rotundity that was to attach to him in future years.
mklmt10{_}2516{_}With the years he prospered increasingly, so that, when he was thirty-six, the promise of his figure was fulfilling rapidly, and, himself a member of the exclusive and powerful Hai Gum Tong, and of the Chinese Merchants' Association, he was accustomed to sitting as host at dinners that cost him as much as thirty years of towing on the eleventh cataract would have earned him.
mklmt10{_}2517{_}Two things he missed: a wife, and his mother to lay the stick on him as of yore.
mklmt10{_}2518{_}When he was thirty-seven he consulted his bank balance.
mklmt10{_}2519{_}It stood him three thousand gold.
mklmt10{_}2520{_}For twenty-five hundred down and an easy mortgage he could buy the three-story shack-building, and the ground in fee simple on which it stood.
mklmt10{_}2521{_}But to do this, left only five hundred for a wife.
mklmt10{_}2522{_}Fu Yee Po had a marriageable, properly small-footed daughter whom he was willing to import from China, and sell to him for eight hundred gold, plus the costs of importation.
mklmt10{_}2523{_}Further, Fu Yee Po was even willing to take five hundred down and the remainder on note at 6 per cent.
mklmt10{_}2524{_}Ah Kim, thirty-seven years of age, fat and a bachelor, really did want a wife, especially a small-footed wife; for, China born and reared, the immemorial small-footed female had been deeply impressed into his fantasy of woman.
mklmt10{_}2525{_}But more, even more and far more than a small-footed wife, did he want his mother and his mother's delectable beatings.
mklmt10{_}2526{_}So he declined Fu Yee Po's easy terms, and at much less cost imported his own mother from servant in a boss coolie's house at a yearly wage of a dollar and a thirty- cent dress to be mistress of his Honolulu three-story shack building with two household servants, three clerks, and a porter of all work under her, to say nothing of ten thousand dollars' worth of dress goods on the shelves that ranged from the cheapest cotton crepes to the most expensive hand-embroidered silks.
mklmt10{_}2527{_}For be it known that even in that early day Ah Kim's emporium was beginning to cater to the tourist trade from the States.
mklmt10{_}2528{_}For thirteen years Ah Kim had lived tolerably happily with his mother, and by her been methodically beaten for causes just or unjust, real or fancied; and at the end of it all he knew as strongly as ever the ache of his heart and head for a wife, and of his loins for sons to live after him, and carry on the dynasty of Ah Kim Company.
mklmt10{_}2529{_}Such the dream that has ever vexed men, from those early ones who first usurped a hunting right, monopolized a sandbar for a fish-trap, or stormed a village and put the males thereof to the sword.
mklmt10{_}2530{_}Kings, millionaires, and Chinese merchants of Honolulu have this in common, despite that they may praise God for having made them differently and in self-likable images.
mklmt10{_}2531{_}And the ideal of woman that Ah Kim at fifty ached for had changed from his ideal at thirty-seven.
mklmt10{_}2532{_}No small-footed wife did he want now, but a free, natural, out-stepping normal-footed woman that, somehow, appeared to him in his day dreams and haunted his night visions in the form of Li Faa, the Silvery Moon Blossom.
mklmt10{_}2533{_}What if she were twice widowed, the daughter of a kanaka mother, the wearer of white-devil skirts and corsets and high-heeled slippers!
mklmt10{_}2534{_}He wanted her.
mklmt10{_}2535{_}It seemed it was written that she should be joint ancestor with him of the line that would continue the ownership and management through the generations, of Ah Kim Company, General Merchandise.
mklmt10{_}2536{_}"I will have no half-pake daughter-in-law," his mother often reiterated to Ah Kim, pake being the Hawaiian word for Chinese.
mklmt10{_}2537{_}"All pake must my daughter-in-law be, even as you, my son, and as I, your mother.
mklmt10{_}2538{_}And she must wear trousers, my son, as all the women of our family before her.
mklmt10{_}2539{_}No woman, in she-devil skirts and corsets, can pay due reverence to our ancestors.
mklmt10{_}2540{_}Corsets and reverence do not go together.
mklmt10{_}2541{_}Such a one is this shameless Li Faa.
mklmt10{_}2542{_}She is impudent and independent, and will be neither obedient to her husband nor her husband's mother.
mklmt10{_}2543{_}This brazen-faced Li Faa would believe herself the source of life and the first ancestor, recognizing no ancestors before her.
mklmt10{_}2544{_}She laughs at our joss- sticks, and paper prayers, and family gods, as I have been well told--"  "Mrs. Chang Lucy," Ah Kim groaned.
mklmt10{_}2545{_}"Not alone Mrs. Chang Lucy, O son.
mklmt10{_}2546{_}I have inquired.
mklmt10{_}2547{_}At least a dozen have heard her say of our joss house that it is all monkey foolishness.
mklmt10{_}2548{_}The words are hers--she, who eats raw fish, raw squid, and baked dog.
mklmt10{_}2549{_}Ours is the foolishness of monkeys.
mklmt10{_}2550{_}Yet would she marry you, a monkey, because of your store that is a palace and of the wealth that makes you a great man.
mklmt10{_}2551{_}And she would put shame on me, and on your father before you long honourably dead."
mklmt10{_}2552{_}And there was no discussing the matter.
mklmt10{_}2553{_}As things were, Ah Kim knew his mother was right.
mklmt10{_}2554{_}Not for nothing had Li Faa been born forty years before of a Chinese father, renegade to all tradition, and of a kanaka mother whose immediate forebears had broken the taboos, cast down their own Polynesian gods, and weak-heartedly listened to the preaching about the remote and unimageable god of the Christian missionaries.
mklmt10{_}2555{_}Li Faa, educated, who could read and write English and Hawaiian and a fair measure of Chinese, claimed to believe in nothing, although in her secret heart she feared the kahunas (Hawaiian witch-doctors), who she was certain could charm away ill luck or pray one to death.
mklmt10{_}2556{_}Li Faa would never come into Ah Kim's house, as he thoroughly knew, and kow-tow to his mother and be slave to her in the immemorial Chinese way.
mklmt10{_}2557{_}Li Faa, from the Chinese angle, was a new woman, a feminist, who rode horseback astride, disported immodestly garbed at Waikiki on the surf-boards, and at more than one luau (feast) had been known to dance the hula with the worst and in excess of the worst, to the scandalous delight of all.
mklmt10{_}2558{_}Ah Kim himself, a generation younger than his mother, had been bitten by the acid of modernity.
mklmt10{_}2559{_}The old order held, in so far as he still felt in his subtlest crypts of being the dusty hand of the past resting on him, residing in him; yet he subscribed to heavy policies of fire and life insurance, acted as treasurer for the local Chinese revolutionises that were for turning the Celestial Empire into a republic, contributed to the funds of the Hawaii-born Chinese baseball nine that excelled the Yankee nines at their own game, talked theosophy with Katso Suguri, the Japanese Buddhist and silk importer, fell for police graft, played and paid his insidious share in the democratic politics of annexed Hawaii, and was thinking of buying an automobile.
mklmt10{_}2560{_}Ah Kim never dared bare himself to himself and thrash out and winnow out how much of the old he had ceased to believe in.
mklmt10{_}2561{_}His mother was of the old, yet he revered her and was happy under her bamboo stick.
mklmt10{_}2562{_}Li Faa, the Silvery Moon Blossom, was of the new, yet he could never be quite completely happy without her.
mklmt10{_}2563{_}For he loved Li Faa.
mklmt10{_}2564{_}Moon-faced, rotund as a water-melon seed, canny business man, wise with half a century of living-- nevertheless Ah Kim became an artist when he thought of her.
mklmt10{_}2565{_}He thought of her in poems of names, as woman transmuted into flower- terms of beauty and philosophic abstractions of achievement and easement.
mklmt10{_}2566{_}She was, to him, and alone to him of all men in the world, his Plum Blossom, his Tranquillity of Woman, his Flower of Serenity, his Moon Lily, and his Perfect Rest.
mklmt10{_}2567{_}And as he murmured these love endearments of namings, it seemed to him that in them were the ripplings of running waters, the tinklings of silver wind- bells, and the scents of the oleander and the jasmine.
mklmt10{_}2568{_}She was his poem of woman, a lyric delight, a three-dimensions of flesh and spirit delicious, a fate and a good fortune written, ere the first man and woman were, by the gods whose whim had been to make all men and women for sorrow and for joy.
mklmt10{_}2569{_}But his mother put into his hand the ink-brush and placed under it, on the table, the writing tablet.
mklmt10{_}2570{_}"Paint," said she, "the ideograph of TO MARRY."
mklmt10{_}2571{_}He obeyed, scarcely wondering, with the deft artistry of his race and training painting the symbolic hieroglyphic.
mklmt10{_}2572{_}"Resolve it," commanded his mother.
mklmt10{_}2573{_}Ah Kim looked at her, curious, willing to please, unaware of the drift of her intent.
mklmt10{_}2574{_}"Of what is it composed?"
mklmt10{_}2575{_}she persisted.
mklmt10{_}2576{_}"What are the three originals, the sum of which is it:  to marry, marriage, the coming together and wedding of a man and a woman?
mklmt10{_}2577{_}Paint them, paint them apart, the three originals, unrelated, so that we may know how the wise men of old wisely built up the ideograph of to marry."
mklmt10{_}2578{_}And Ah Kim, obeying and painting, saw that what he had painted were three picture-signs--the picture-signs of a hand, an ear, and a woman.
mklmt10{_}2579{_}"Name them," said his mother; and he named them.
mklmt10{_}2580{_}"It is true," said she.
mklmt10{_}2581{_}"It is a great tale.
mklmt10{_}2582{_}It is the stuff of the painted pictures of marriage.
mklmt10{_}2583{_}Such marriage was in the beginning; such shall it always be in my house.
mklmt10{_}2584{_}The hand of the man takes the woman's ear, and by it leads her away to his house, where she is to be obedient to him and to his mother.
mklmt10{_}2585{_}I was taken by the ear, so, by your long honourably dead father.
mklmt10{_}2586{_}I have looked at your hand.
mklmt10{_}2587{_}It is not like his hand.
mklmt10{_}2588{_}Also have I looked at the ear of Li Faa.
mklmt10{_}2589{_}Never will you lead her by the ear.
mklmt10{_}2590{_}She has not that kind of an ear.
mklmt10{_}2591{_}I shall live a long time yet, and I will be mistress in my son's house, after our ancient way, until I die."
mklmt10{_}2592{_}"But she is my revered ancestress," Ah Kim explained to Li Faa.
mklmt10{_}2593{_}He was timidly unhappy; for Li Faa, having ascertained that Mrs. Tai Fu was at the temple of the Chinese AEsculapius making a food offering of dried duck and prayers for her declining health, had taken advantage of the opportunity to call upon him in his store.
mklmt10{_}2594{_}Li Faa pursed her insolent, unpainted lips into the form of a half- opened rosebud, and replied:  "That will do for China.
mklmt10{_}2595{_}I do not know China.
mklmt10{_}2596{_}This is Hawaii, and in Hawaii the customs of all foreigners change."
mklmt10{_}2597{_}"She is nevertheless my ancestress," Ah Kim protested, "the mother who gave me birth, whether I am in China or Hawaii, O Silvery Moon Blossom that I want for wife."
mklmt10{_}2598{_}"I have had two husbands," Li Faa stated placidly.
mklmt10{_}2599{_}"One was a pake, one was a Portuguese.
mklmt10{_}2600{_}I learned much from both.
mklmt10{_}2601{_}Also am I educated.
mklmt10{_}2602{_}I have been to High School, and I have played the piano in public.
mklmt10{_}2603{_}And I learned from my two husbands much.
mklmt10{_}2604{_}The pake makes the best husband.
mklmt10{_}2605{_}Never again will I marry anything but a pake.
mklmt10{_}2606{_}But he must not take me by the ear--"  "How do you know of that?"
mklmt10{_}2607{_}he broke in suspiciously.
mklmt10{_}2608{_}"Mrs. Chang Lucy," was the reply.
mklmt10{_}2609{_}"Mrs. Chang Lucy tells me everything that your mother tells her, and your mother tells her much.
mklmt10{_}2610{_}So let me tell you that mine is not that kind of an ear."
mklmt10{_}2611{_}"Which is what my honoured mother has told me," Ah Kim groaned.
mklmt10{_}2612{_}"Which is what your honoured mother told Mrs. Chang Lucy, which is what Mrs. Chang Lucy told me," Li Faa completed equably.
mklmt10{_}2613{_}"And I now tell you, O Third Husband To Be, that the man is not born who will lead me by the ear.
mklmt10{_}2614{_}It is not the way in Hawaii.
mklmt10{_}2615{_}I will go only hand in hand with my man, side by side, fifty-fifty as is the haole slang just now.
mklmt10{_}2616{_}My Portuguese husband thought different.
mklmt10{_}2617{_}He tried to beat me.
mklmt10{_}2618{_}I landed him three times in the police court and each time he worked out his sentence on the reef.
mklmt10{_}2619{_}After that he got drowned."
mklmt10{_}2620{_}"My mother has been my mother for fifty years," Ah Kim declared stoutly.
mklmt10{_}2621{_}"And for fifty years has she beaten you," Li Faa giggled.
mklmt10{_}2622{_}"How my father used to laugh at Yap Ten Shin!
mklmt10{_}2623{_}Like you, Yap Ten Shin had been born in China, and had brought the China customs with him.
mklmt10{_}2624{_}His old father was for ever beating him with a stick.
mklmt10{_}2625{_}He loved his father.
mklmt10{_}2626{_}But his father beat him harder than ever when he became a missionary pake.
mklmt10{_}2627{_}Every time he went to the missionary services, his father beat him.
mklmt10{_}2628{_}And every time the missionary heard of it he was harsh in his language to Yap Ten Shin for allowing his father to beat him.
mklmt10{_}2629{_}And my father laughed and laughed, for my father was a very liberal pake, who had changed his customs quicker than most foreigners.
mklmt10{_}2630{_}And all the trouble was because Yap Ten Shin had a loving heart.
mklmt10{_}2631{_}He loved his honourable father.
mklmt10{_}2632{_}He loved the God of Love of the Christian missionary.
mklmt10{_}2633{_}But in the end, in me, he found the greatest love of all, which is the love of woman.
mklmt10{_}2634{_}In me he forgot his love for his father and his love for the loving Christ.
mklmt10{_}2635{_}"And he offered my father six hundred gold, for me--the price was small because my feet were not small.
mklmt10{_}2636{_}But I was half kanaka.
mklmt10{_}2637{_}I said that I was not a slave-woman, and that I would be sold to no man.
mklmt10{_}2638{_}My high-school teacher was a haole old maid who said love of woman was so beyond price that it must never be sold.
mklmt10{_}2639{_}Perhaps that is why she was an old maid.
mklmt10{_}2640{_}She was not beautiful.
mklmt10{_}2641{_}She could not give herself away.
mklmt10{_}2642{_}My kanaka mother said it was not the kanaka way to sell their daughters for a money price.
mklmt10{_}2643{_}They gave their daughters for love, and she would listen to reason if Yap Ten Shin provided luaus in quantity and quality.
mklmt10{_}2644{_}My pake father, as I have told you, was liberal.
mklmt10{_}2645{_}He asked me if I wanted Yap Ten Shin for my husband.
mklmt10{_}2646{_}And I said yes; and freely, of myself, I went to him.
mklmt10{_}2647{_}He it was who was kicked by a horse; but he was a very good husband before he was kicked by the horse.
mklmt10{_}2648{_}"As for you, Ah Kim, you shall always be honourable and lovable for me, and some day, when it is not necessary for you to take me by the ear, I shall marry you and come here and be with you always, and you will be the happiest pake in all Hawaii; for I have had two husbands, and gone to high school, and am most wise in making a husband happy.
mklmt10{_}2649{_}But that will be when your mother has ceased to beat you.
mklmt10{_}2650{_}Mrs. Chang Lucy tells me that she beats you very hard."
mklmt10{_}2651{_}"She does," Ah Kim affirmed.
mklmt10{_}2652{_}"Behold!
mklmt10{_}2653{_}He thrust back his loose sleeves, exposing to the elbow his smooth and cherubic forearms.
mklmt10{_}2654{_}They were mantled with black and blue marks that advertised the weight and number of blows so shielded from his head and face.
mklmt10{_}2655{_}"But she has never made me cry," Ah Kim disclaimed hastily.
mklmt10{_}2656{_}"Never, from the time I was a little boy, has she made me cry."
mklmt10{_}2657{_}"So Mrs. Chang Lucy says," Li Faa observed.
mklmt10{_}2658{_}"She says that your honourable mother often complains to her that she has never made you cry."
mklmt10{_}2659{_}A sibilant warning from one of his clerks was too late.
mklmt10{_}2660{_}Having regained the house by way of the back alley, Mrs. Tai Fu emerged right upon them from out of the living apartments.
mklmt10{_}2661{_}Never had Ah Kim seen his mother's eyes so blazing furious.
mklmt10{_}2662{_}She ignored Li Faa, as she screamed at him:  "Now will I make you cry.
mklmt10{_}2663{_}As never before shall I beat you until you do cry."
mklmt10{_}2664{_}"Then let us go into the back rooms, honourable mother," Ah Kim suggested.
mklmt10{_}2665{_}"We will close the windows and the doors, and there may you beat me."
mklmt10{_}2666{_}"No.
mklmt10{_}2667{_}Here shall you be beaten before all the world and this shameless woman who would, with her own hand, take you by the ear and call such sacrilege marriage!
mklmt10{_}2668{_}Stay, shameless woman."
mklmt10{_}2669{_}"I am going to stay anyway," said Li Faa.
mklmt10{_}2670{_}She favoured the clerks with a truculent stare.
mklmt10{_}2671{_}"And I'd like to see anything less than the police put me out of here."
mklmt10{_}2672{_}"You will never be my daughter-in-law," Mrs. Tai Fu snapped.
mklmt10{_}2673{_}Li Faa nodded her head in agreement.
mklmt10{_}2674{_}"But just the same," she added, "shall your son be my third husband."
mklmt10{_}2675{_}"You mean when I am dead?"
mklmt10{_}2676{_}the old mother screamed.
mklmt10{_}2677{_}"The sun rises each morning," Li Faa said enigmatically.
mklmt10{_}2678{_}"All my life have I seen it rise--"  "You are forty, and you wear corsets."
mklmt10{_}2679{_}"But I do not dye my hair--that will come later," Li Faa calmly retorted.
mklmt10{_}2680{_}"As to my age, you are right.
mklmt10{_}2681{_}I shall be forty-one next Kamehameha Day.
mklmt10{_}2682{_}For forty years I have seen the sun rise.
mklmt10{_}2683{_}My father was an old man.
mklmt10{_}2684{_}Before he died he told me that he had observed no difference in the rising of the sun since when he was a little boy.
mklmt10{_}2685{_}The world is round.
mklmt10{_}2686{_}Confucius did not know that, but you will find it in all the geography books.
mklmt10{_}2687{_}The world is round.
mklmt10{_}2688{_}Ever it turns over on itself, over and over and around and around.
mklmt10{_}2689{_}And the times and seasons of weather and life turn with it.
mklmt10{_}2690{_}What is, has been before.
mklmt10{_}2691{_}What has been, will be again.
mklmt10{_}2692{_}The time of the breadfruit and the mango ever recurs, and man and woman repeat themselves.
mklmt10{_}2693{_}The robins nest, and in the springtime the plovers come from the north.
mklmt10{_}2694{_}Every spring is followed by another spring.
mklmt10{_}2695{_}The coconut palm rises into the air, ripens its fruit, and departs.
mklmt10{_}2696{_}But always are there more coconut palms.
mklmt10{_}2697{_}This is not all my own smart talk.
mklmt10{_}2698{_}Much of it my father told me.
mklmt10{_}2699{_}Proceed, honourable Mrs. Tai Fu, and beat your son who is my Third Husband To Be.
mklmt10{_}2700{_}But I shall laugh.
mklmt10{_}2701{_}I warn you I shall laugh."
mklmt10{_}2702{_}Ah Kim dropped down on his knees so as to give his mother every advantage.
mklmt10{_}2703{_}And while she rained blows upon him with the bamboo stick, Li Faa smiled and giggled, and finally burst into laughter.
mklmt10{_}2704{_}"Harder, O honourable Mrs. Tai Fu!"
mklmt10{_}2705{_}Li Faa urged between paroxysms of mirth.
mklmt10{_}2706{_}Mrs. Tai Fu did her best, which was notably weak, until she observed what made her drop the stick by her side in amazement.
mklmt10{_}2707{_}Ah Kim was crying.
mklmt10{_}2708{_}Down both cheeks great round tears were coursing.
mklmt10{_}2709{_}Li Faa was amazed.
mklmt10{_}2710{_}So were the gaping clerks.
mklmt10{_}2711{_}Most amazed of all was Ah Kim, yet he could not help himself; and, although no further blows fell, he cried steadily on.
mklmt10{_}2712{_}"But why did you cry?"
mklmt10{_}2713{_}Li Faa demanded often of Ah Kim.
mklmt10{_}2714{_}"It was so perfectly foolish a thing to do.
mklmt10{_}2715{_}She was not even hurting you."
mklmt10{_}2716{_}"Wait until we are married," was Ah Kim's invariable reply, "and then, O Moon Lily, will I tell you."
mklmt10{_}2717{_}Two years later, one afternoon, more like a water-melon seed in configuration than ever, Ah Kim returned home from a meeting of the Chinese Protective Association, to find his mother dead on her couch.
mklmt10{_}2718{_}Narrower and more unrelenting than ever were the forehead and the brushed-back hair.
mklmt10{_}2719{_}But on her face was a withered smile.
mklmt10{_}2720{_}The gods had been kind.
mklmt10{_}2721{_}She had passed without pain.
mklmt10{_}2722{_}He telephoned first of all to Li Faa's number but did not find her until he called up Mrs. Chang Lucy.
mklmt10{_}2723{_}The news given, the marriage was dated ahead with ten times the brevity of the old-line Chinese custom.
mklmt10{_}2724{_}And if there be anything analogous to a bridesmaid in a Chinese wedding, Mrs. Chang Lucy was just that.
mklmt10{_}2725{_}"Why," Li Faa asked Ah Kim when alone with him on their wedding night, "why did you cry when your mother beat you that day in the store?
mklmt10{_}2726{_}You were so foolish.
mklmt10{_}2727{_}She was not even hurting you."
mklmt10{_}2728{_}"That is why I cried," answered Ah Kim.
mklmt10{_}2729{_}Li Faa looked up at him without understanding.
mklmt10{_}2730{_}"I cried," he explained, "because I suddenly knew that my mother was nearing her end.
mklmt10{_}2731{_}There was no weight, no hurt, in her blows.
mklmt10{_}2732{_}I cried because I knew SHE NO LONGER HAD STRENGTH ENOUGH TO HURT ME.
mklmt10{_}2733{_}That is why I cried, my Flower of Serenity, my Perfect Rest.
mklmt10{_}2734{_}That is the only reason why I cried."
mklmt10{_}2735{_}WAIKIKI, HONOLULU.
mklmt10{_}2736{_}June 16, 1916.
mklmt10{_}2737{_}THE KANAKA SURF    The tourist women, under the hau tree arbour that lines the Moana hotel beach, gasped when Lee Barton and his wife Ida emerged from the bath-house.
mklmt10{_}2738{_}And as the pair walked past them and down to the sand, they continued to gasp.
mklmt10{_}2739{_}Not that there was anything about Lee Barton provocative of gasps.
mklmt10{_}2740{_}The tourist women were not of the sort to gasp at sight of a mere man's swimming-suited body, no matter with what swelling splendour of line and muscle such body was invested.
mklmt10{_}2741{_}Nevertheless, trainers and conditioners of men would have drawn deep breaths of satisfaction at contemplation of the physical spectacle of him.
mklmt10{_}2742{_}But they would not have gasped in the way the women did, whose gasps were indicative of moral shock.
mklmt10{_}2743{_}Ida Barton was the cause of their perturbation and disapproval.
mklmt10{_}2744{_}They disapproved, seriously so, at the first instant's glimpse of her.
mklmt10{_}2745{_}They thought--such ardent self-deceivers were they--that they were shocked by her swimming suit.
mklmt10{_}2746{_}But Freud has pointed out how persons, where sex is involved, are prone sincerely to substitute one thing for another thing, and to agonize over the substituted thing as strenuously as if it were the real thing.
mklmt10{_}2747{_}Ida Barton's swimming suit was a very nice one, as women's suits go.
mklmt10{_}2748{_}Of thinnest of firm-woven black wool, with white trimmings and a white belt-line, it was high-throated, short-sleeved, and brief- skirted.
mklmt10{_}2749{_}Brief as was the skirt, the leg-tights were no less brief.
mklmt10{_}2750{_}Yet on the beach in front of the adjacent Outrigger Club, and entering and leaving the water, a score of women, not provoking gasping notice, were more daringly garbed.
mklmt10{_}2751{_}Their men's suits, as brief of leg-tights and skirts, fitted them as snugly, but were sleeveless after the way of men's suits, the arm-holes deeply low- cut and in-cut, and, by the exposed armpits, advertiseful that the wearers were accustomed to 1916 decollete.
mklmt10{_}2752{_}So it was not Ida Barton's suit, although the women deceived themselves into thinking it was.
mklmt10{_}2753{_}It was, first of all, say her legs; or, first of all, say the totality of her, the sweet and brilliant jewel of her femininity bursting upon them.
mklmt10{_}2754{_}Dowager, matron, and maid, conserving their soft-fat muscles or protecting their hot-house complexions in the shade of the hau-tree arbour, felt the immediate challenge of her.
mklmt10{_}2755{_}She was menace as well, an affront of superiority in their own chosen and variously successful game of life.
mklmt10{_}2756{_}But they did not say it.
mklmt10{_}2757{_}They did not permit themselves to think it.
mklmt10{_}2758{_}They thought it was the suit, and said so to one another, ignoring the twenty women more daringly clad but less perilously beautiful.
mklmt10{_}2759{_}Could one have winnowed out of the souls of these disapproving ones what lay at bottom of their condemnation of her suit, it would have been found to be the sex-jealous thought:  THAT NO WOMAN, SO BEAUTIFUL AS THIS ONE, SHOULD BE PERMITTED TO SHOW HER BEAUTY.
mklmt10{_}2760{_}It was not fair to them.
mklmt10{_}2761{_}What chance had they in the conquering of males with so dangerous a rival in the foreground?
mklmt10{_}2762{_}They were justified.
mklmt10{_}2763{_}As Stanley Patterson said to his wife, where the two of them lolled wet in the sand by the tiny fresh-water stream that the Bartons waded in order to gain the Outrigger Club beach:  "Lord god of models and marvels, behold them!
mklmt10{_}2764{_}My dear, did you ever see two such legs on one small woman!
mklmt10{_}2765{_}Look at the roundness and taperingness.
mklmt10{_}2766{_}They're boy's legs.
mklmt10{_}2767{_}I've seen featherweights go into the ring with legs like those.
mklmt10{_}2768{_}And they're all-woman's legs, too.
mklmt10{_}2769{_}Never mistake them in the world.
mklmt10{_}2770{_}The arc of the front line of that upper leg!
mklmt10{_}2771{_}And the balanced adequate fullness at the back!
mklmt10{_}2772{_}And the way the opposing curves slender in to the knee that IS a knee!
mklmt10{_}2773{_}Makes my fingers itch.
mklmt10{_}2774{_}Wish I had some clay right now."
mklmt10{_}2775{_}"It's a true human knee," his wife concurred, no less breathlessly; for, like her husband, she was a sculptor.
mklmt10{_}2776{_}"Look at the joint of it working under the skin.
mklmt10{_}2777{_}It's got form, and blessedly is not covered by a bag of fat."
mklmt10{_}2778{_}She paused to sigh, thinking of her own knees.
mklmt10{_}2779{_}"It's correct, and beautiful, and dainty.
mklmt10{_}2780{_}Charm!
mklmt10{_}2781{_}If ever I beheld the charm of flesh, it is now.
mklmt10{_}2782{_}I wonder who she is."
mklmt10{_}2783{_}Stanley Patterson, gazing ardently, took up his half of the chorus.
mklmt10{_}2784{_}"Notice that the round muscle-pads on the inner sides that make most women appear knock-kneed are missing.
mklmt10{_}2785{_}They're boy's legs, firm and sure--"  "And sweet woman's legs, soft and round," his wife hastened to balance.
mklmt10{_}2786{_}"And look, Stanley!
mklmt10{_}2787{_}See how she walks on the balls of her feet.
mklmt10{_}2788{_}It makes her seem light as swan's down.
mklmt10{_}2789{_}Each step seems just a little above the earth, and each other step seems just a little higher above until you get the impression she is flying, or just about to rise and begin flying .
mklmt10{_}2790{_}.
mklmt10{_}2791{_}. "
mklmt10{_}2792{_}So Stanley and Mrs. Patterson.
mklmt10{_}2793{_}But they were artists, with eyes therefore unlike the next batteries of human eyes Ida Barton was compelled to run, and that laired on the Outrigger lanais (verandas) and in the hau-tree shade of the closely adjoining seaside.
mklmt10{_}2794{_}The majority of the Outrigger audience was composed, not of tourist guests, but of club members and old-timers in Hawaii.
mklmt10{_}2795{_}And even the old-times women gasped.
mklmt10{_}2796{_}"It's positively indecent," said Mrs. Hanley Black to her husband, herself a too-stout-in-the-middle matron of forty-five, who had been born in the Hawaiian islands, and who had never heard of Ostend.
mklmt10{_}2797{_}Hanley Black surveyed his wife's criminal shapelessness and voluminousness of antediluvian, New-England swimming dress with a withering, contemplative eye.
mklmt10{_}2798{_}They had been married a sufficient number of years for him frankly to utter his judgment.
mklmt10{_}2799{_}"That strange woman's suit makes your own look indecent.
mklmt10{_}2800{_}You appear as a creature shameful, under a grotesqueness of apparel striving to hide some secret awfulness."
mklmt10{_}2801{_}"She carries her body like a Spanish dancer," Mrs. Patterson said to her husband, for the pair of them had waded the little stream in pursuit of the vision.
mklmt10{_}2802{_}"By George, she does," Stanley Patterson concurred.
mklmt10{_}2803{_}"Reminds me of Estrellita.
mklmt10{_}2804{_}Torso just well enough forward, slender waist, not too lean in the stomach, and with muscles like some lad boxer's armouring that stomach to fearlessness.
mklmt10{_}2805{_}She has to have them to carry herself that way and to balance the back muscles.
mklmt10{_}2806{_}See that muscled curve of the back!
mklmt10{_}2807{_}It's Estrellita's."
mklmt10{_}2808{_}"How tall would you say?"
mklmt10{_}2809{_}his wife queried.
mklmt10{_}2810{_}"There she deceives," was the appraised answer.
mklmt10{_}2811{_}"She might be five-feet-one, or five-feet-three or four.
mklmt10{_}2812{_}It's that way she has of walking that you described as almost about to fly."
mklmt10{_}2813{_}"Yes, that's it," Mrs. Patterson concurred.
mklmt10{_}2814{_}"It's her energy, her seemingness of being on tip toe with rising vitality."
mklmt10{_}2815{_}Stanley Patterson considered for a space.
mklmt10{_}2816{_}"That's it," he enounced.
mklmt10{_}2817{_}"She IS a little thing.
mklmt10{_}2818{_}I'll give her five-two in her stockings.
mklmt10{_}2819{_}And I'll weigh her a mere one hundred and ten, or eight, or fifteen at the outside."
mklmt10{_}2820{_}"She won't weigh a hundred and ten," his wife declared with conviction.
mklmt10{_}2821{_}"And with her clothes on, plus her carriage (which is builded of her vitality and will), I'll wager she'd never impress any one with her smallness."
mklmt10{_}2822{_}"I know her type," his wife nodded.
mklmt10{_}2823{_}"You meet her out, and you have the sense that, while not exactly a fine large woman, she's a whole lot larger than the average.
mklmt10{_}2824{_}And now, age?"
mklmt10{_}2825{_}"I'll give you best there," he parried.
mklmt10{_}2826{_}"She might be twenty-five, she might be twenty-eight .
mklmt10{_}2827{_}.
mklmt10{_}2828{_}. "
mklmt10{_}2829{_}But Stanley Patterson had impolitely forgotten to listen.
mklmt10{_}2830{_}"It's not her legs alone," he cried on enthusiastically.
mklmt10{_}2831{_}"It's the all of her.
mklmt10{_}2832{_}Look at the delicacy of that forearm.
mklmt10{_}2833{_}And the swell of line to the shoulder.
mklmt10{_}2834{_}And that biceps!
mklmt10{_}2835{_}It's alive.
mklmt10{_}2836{_}Dollars to drowned kittens she can flex a respectable knot of it .
mklmt10{_}2837{_}.
mklmt10{_}2838{_}. "
mklmt10{_}2839{_}No woman, much less an Ida Barton, could have been unconscious of the effect she was producing along Waikiki Beach.
mklmt10{_}2840{_}Instead of making her happy in the small vanity way, it irritated her.
mklmt10{_}2841{_}"The cats," she laughed to her husband.
mklmt10{_}2842{_}"And to think I was born here an almost even third of a century ago!
mklmt10{_}2843{_}But they weren't nasty then.
mklmt10{_}2844{_}Maybe because there weren't any tourists.
mklmt10{_}2845{_}Why, Lee, I learned to swim right here on this beach in front of the Outrigger.
mklmt10{_}2846{_}We used to come out with daddy for vacations and for week-ends and sort of camp out in a grass house that stood right where the Outrigger ladies serve tea now.
mklmt10{_}2847{_}And centipedes fell out of the thatch on us, while we slept, and we all ate poi and opihis and raw aku, and nobody wore much of anything for the swimming and squidding, and there was no real road to town.
mklmt10{_}2848{_}I remember times of big rain when it was so flooded we had to go in by canoe, out through the reef and in by Honolulu Harbour."
mklmt10{_}2849{_}"Remember," Lee Barton added, "it was just about that time that the youngster that became me arrived here for a few weeks' stay on our way around.
mklmt10{_}2850{_}I must have seen you on the beach at that very time-- one of the kiddies that swam like fishes.
mklmt10{_}2851{_}Why, merciful me, the women here were all riding cross-saddle, and that was long before the rest of the social female world outgrew its immodesty and came around to sitting simultaneously on both sides of a horse.
mklmt10{_}2852{_}I learned to swim on the beach here at that time myself.
mklmt10{_}2853{_}You and I may even have tried body-surfing on the same waves, or I may have splashed a handful of water into your mouth and been rewarded by your sticking out your tongue at me--"  Interrupted by an audible gasp of shock from a spinster-appearing female sunning herself hard by and angularly in the sand in a swimming suit monstrously unbeautiful, Lee Barton was aware of an involuntary and almost perceptible stiffening on the part of his wife.
mklmt10{_}2854{_}"I smile with pleasure," he told her.
mklmt10{_}2855{_}"It serves only to make your valiant little shoulders the more valiant.
mklmt10{_}2856{_}It may make you self- conscious, but it likewise makes you absurdly self-confident."
mklmt10{_}2857{_}For, be it known in advance, Lee Barton was a super-man and Ida Barton a super-woman--or at least they were personalities so designated by the cub book-reviewers, flat-floor men and women, and scholastically emasculated critics, who from across the dreary levels of their living can descry no glorious humans over-topping their horizons.
mklmt10{_}2858{_}These dreary folk, echoes of the dead past and importunate and self-elected pall-bearers for the present and future, proxy-livers of life and vicarious sensualists that they are in a eunuch sort of way, insist, since their own selves, environments, and narrow agitations of the quick are mediocre and commonplace, that no man or woman can rise above the mediocre and commonplace.
mklmt10{_}2859{_}Lacking gloriousness in themselves, they deny gloriousness to all mankind; too cowardly for whimsy and derring-do, they assert whimsy and derring-do ceased at the very latest no later than the middle ages; flickering little tapers themselves, their feeble eyes are dazzled to unseeingness of the flaming conflagrations of other souls that illumine their skies.
mklmt10{_}2860{_}Possessing power in no greater quantity than is the just due of pygmies, they cannot conceive of power greater in others than in themselves.
mklmt10{_}2861{_}In those days there were giants; but, as their mouldy books tell them, the giants are long since passed, and only the bones of them remain.
mklmt10{_}2862{_}Never having seen the mountains, there are no mountains.
mklmt10{_}2863{_}In the mud of their complacently perpetuated barnyard pond, they assert that no bright-browed, bright-apparelled shining figures can be outside of fairy books, old histories, and ancient superstitions.
mklmt10{_}2864{_}Never having seen the stars, they deny the stars.
mklmt10{_}2865{_}Never having glimpsed the shining ways nor the mortals that tread them, they deny the existence of the shinning ways as well as the existence of the high-bright mortals who adventure along the shining ways.
mklmt10{_}2866{_}The narrow pupils of their eyes the centre of the universe, they image the universe in terms of themselves, of their meagre personalities make pitiful yardsticks with which to measure the high-bright souls, saying:  "Thus long are all souls, and no longer; it is impossible that there should exist greater-statured souls than we are, and our gods know that we are great of stature."
mklmt10{_}2867{_}But all, or nearly all on the beach, forgave Ida Barton her suit and form when she took the water.
mklmt10{_}2868{_}A touch of her hand on her husband's arm, indication and challenge in her laughing face, and the two ran as one for half a dozen paces and leapt as one from the hard-wet sand of the beach, their bodies describing flat arches of flight ere the water was entered.
mklmt10{_}2869{_}There are two surfs at Waikiki:  the big, bearded man surf that roars far out beyond the diving-stage; the smaller, gentler, wahine, or woman, surf that breaks upon the shore itself.
mklmt10{_}2870{_}Here is a great shallowness, where one may wade a hundred or several hundred feet to get beyond depth.
mklmt10{_}2871{_}Yet, with a good surf on outside, the wahine surf can break three or four feet, so that, close in against the shore, the hard-sand bottom may be three feet or three inches under the welter of surface foam.
mklmt10{_}2872{_}To dive from the beach into this, to fly into the air off racing feet, turn in mid- flight so that heels are up and head is down, and, so to enter the water head-first, requires wisdom of waves, timing of waves, and a trained deftness in entering such unstable depths of water with pretty, unapprehensive, head-first cleavage, while at the same time making the shallowest possible of dives.
mklmt10{_}2873{_}It is a sweet, and pretty, and daring trick, not learned in a day, nor learned at all without many a milder bump on the bottom or close shave of fractured skull or broken neck.
mklmt10{_}2874{_}Here, on the spot where the Bartons so beautifully dived, two days before a Stanford track athlete had broken his neck.
mklmt10{_}2875{_}His had been an error in timing the rise and subsidence of a wahine wave.
mklmt10{_}2876{_}"A professional," Mrs. Hanley Black sneered to her husband at Ida Barton's feat.
mklmt10{_}2877{_}"Some vaudeville tank girl," was one of the similar remarks with which the women in the shade complacently reassured one another-- finding, by way of the weird mental processes of self-illusion, a great satisfaction in the money caste-distinction between one who worked for what she ate and themselves who did not work for what they ate.
mklmt10{_}2878{_}It was a day of heavy surf on Waikiki.
mklmt10{_}2879{_}In the wahine surf it was boisterous enough for good swimmers.
mklmt10{_}2880{_}But out beyond, in the kanaka, or man, surf, no one ventured.
mklmt10{_}2881{_}Not that the score or more of young surf-riders loafing on the beach could not venture there, or were afraid to venture there; but because their biggest outrigger canoes would have been swamped, and their surf-boards would have been overwhelmed in the too-immense over-topple and down-fall of the thundering monsters.
mklmt10{_}2882{_}They themselves, most of them, could have swum, for man can swim through breakers which canoes and surf-boards cannot surmount; but to ride the backs of the waves, rise out of the foam to stand full length in the air above, and with heels winged with the swiftness of horses to fly shoreward, was what made sport for them and brought them out from Honolulu to Waikiki.
mklmt10{_}2883{_}The captain of Number Nine canoe, himself a charter member of the Outrigger and a many-times medallist in long-distance swimming, had missed seeing the Bartons take the water, and first glimpsed them beyond the last festoon of bathers clinging to the life-lines.
mklmt10{_}2884{_}From then on, from his vantage of the upstairs lanai, he kept his eyes on them.
mklmt10{_}2885{_}When they continued out past the steel diving-stage where a few of the hardiest divers disported, he muttered vexedly under his breath "damned malahinis!"
mklmt10{_}2886{_}Now malahini means new-comer, tender-foot; and, despite the prettiness of their stroke, he knew that none except malahinis would venture into the racing channel beyond the diving-stage.
mklmt10{_}2887{_}Hence the vexation of the captain of Number Nine.
mklmt10{_}2888{_}He descended to the beach, with a low word here and there picked a crew of the strongest surfers, and returned to the lanai with a pair of binoculars.
mklmt10{_}2889{_}Quite casually, the crew, six of them, carried Number Nine to the water's edge, saw paddles and everything in order for a quick launching, and lolled about carelessly on the sand.
mklmt10{_}2890{_}They were guilty of not advertising that anything untoward was afoot, although they did steal glances up to their captain straining through the binoculars.
mklmt10{_}2891{_}What made the channel was the fresh-water stream.
mklmt10{_}2892{_}Coral cannot abide fresh water.
mklmt10{_}2893{_}What made the channel race was the immense shoreward surf-fling of the sea.
mklmt10{_}2894{_}Unable to remain flung up on the beach, pounded ever back toward the beach by the perpetual shoreward rush of the kanaka surf, the up-piled water escaped to the sea by way of the channel and in the form of under-tow along the bottom under the breakers.
mklmt10{_}2895{_}Even in the channel the waves broke big, but not with the magnificent bigness of terror as to right and left.
mklmt10{_}2896{_}So it was that a canoe or a comparatively strong swimmer could dare the channel.
mklmt10{_}2897{_}But the swimmer must be a strong swimmer indeed, who could successfully buck the current in.
mklmt10{_}2898{_}Wherefore the captain of Number Nine continued his vigil and his muttered damnation of malahinis, disgustedly sure that these two malahinis would compel him to launch Number Nine and go after them when they found the current too strong to swim in against.
mklmt10{_}2899{_}As for himself, caught in their predicament, he would have veered to the left toward Diamond Head and come in on the shoreward fling of the kanaka surf.
mklmt10{_}2900{_}But then, he was no one other than himself, a bronze.
mklmt10{_}2901{_}Hercules of twenty-two, the whitest blond man ever burned to mahogany brown by a sub-tropic sun, with body and lines and muscles very much resembling the wonderful ones of Duke Kahanamoku.
mklmt10{_}2902{_}In a hundred yards the world champion could invariably beat him a second flat; but over a distance of miles he could swim circles around the champion.
mklmt10{_}2903{_}No one of the many hundreds on the beach, with the exception of till captain and his crew, knew that the Bartons had passed beyond the diving-stage.
mklmt10{_}2904{_}All who had watched them start to swim out had taken for granted that they had joined the others on the stage.
mklmt10{_}2905{_}The captain suddenly sprang upon the railing of the lanai, held on to a pillar with one hand, and again picked up the two specks of heads through the glasses.
mklmt10{_}2906{_}His surprise was verified.
mklmt10{_}2907{_}The two fools had veered out of the channel toward Diamond Head, and were directly seaward of the kanaka surf.
mklmt10{_}2908{_}Worse, as he looked, they were starting to come in through the kanaka surf.
mklmt10{_}2909{_}He glanced down quickly to the canoe, and even as he glanced, and as the apparently loafing members quietly arose and took their places by the canoe for the launching, he achieved judgment.
mklmt10{_}2910{_}Before the canoe could get abreast in the channel, all would be over with the man and woman.
mklmt10{_}2911{_}And, granted that it could get abreast of them, the moment it ventured into the kanaka surf it would be swamped, and a sorry chance would the strongest swimmer of them have of rescuing a person pounding to pulp on the bottom under the smashes of the great bearded ones.
mklmt10{_}2912{_}The captain saw the first kanaka wave, large of itself, but small among its fellows, lift seaward behind the two speck-swimmers.
mklmt10{_}2913{_}Then he saw them strike a crawl-stroke, side by side, faces downward, full-lengths out-stretched on surface, their feet sculling like propellers and their arms flailing in rapid over-hand strokes, as they spurted speed to approximate the speed of the overtaking wave, so that, when overtaken, they would become part of the wave, and travel with it instead of being left behind it.
mklmt10{_}2914{_}Thus, if they were coolly skilled enough to ride outstretched on the surface and the forward face of the crest instead of being flung and crumpled or driven head-first to bottom, they would dash shoreward, not propelled by their own energy, but by the energy of the wave into which they had become incorporated.
mklmt10{_}2915{_}And they did it!
mklmt10{_}2916{_}"SOME swimmers!"
mklmt10{_}2917{_}the captain of Number Nine made announcement to himself under his breath.
mklmt10{_}2918{_}He continued to gaze eagerly.
mklmt10{_}2919{_}The best of swimmers could hold such a wave for several hundred feet.
mklmt10{_}2920{_}But could they?
mklmt10{_}2921{_}If they did, they would be a third of the way through the perils they had challenged.
mklmt10{_}2922{_}But, not unexpected by him, the woman failed first, her body not presenting the larger surfaces that her husband's did.
mklmt10{_}2923{_}At the end of seventy feet she was overwhelmed, being driven downward and out of sight by the tons of water in the over-topple.
mklmt10{_}2924{_}Her husband followed and both appeared swimming beyond the wave they had lost.
mklmt10{_}2925{_}The captain saw the next wave first.
mklmt10{_}2926{_}"If they try to body-surf on that, good night," he muttered; for he knew the swimmer did not live who would tackle it.
mklmt10{_}2927{_}Beardless itself, it was father of all bearded ones, a mile long, rising up far out beyond where the others rose, towering its solid bulk higher and higher till it blotted out the horizon, and was a giant among its fellows ere its beard began to grow as it thinned its crest to the over-curl.
mklmt10{_}2928{_}But it was evident that the man and woman knew big water.
mklmt10{_}2929{_}No racing stroke did they make in advance of the wave.
mklmt10{_}2930{_}The captain inwardly applauded as he saw them turn and face the wave and wait for it.
mklmt10{_}2931{_}It was a picture that of all on the beach he alone saw, wonderfully distinct and vivid in the magnification of the binoculars.
mklmt10{_}2932{_}The wall of the wave was truly a wall, mounting, ever mounting, and thinning, far up, to a transparency of the colours of the setting sun shooting athwart all the green and blue of it.
mklmt10{_}2933{_}The green thinned to lighter green that merged blue even as he looked.
mklmt10{_}2934{_}But it was a blue gem-brilliant with innumerable sparkle-points of rose and gold flashed through it by the sun.
mklmt10{_}2935{_}On and up, to the sprouting beard of growing crest, the colour orgy increased until it was a kaleidoscopic effervescence of transfusing rainbows.
mklmt10{_}2936{_}Against the face of the wave showed the heads of the man and woman like two sheer specks.
mklmt10{_}2937{_}Specks they were, of the quick, adventuring among the blind elemental forces, daring the titanic buffets of the sea.
mklmt10{_}2938{_}The weight of the down-fall of that father of waves, even then imminent above their heads, could stun a man or break the fragile bones of a woman.
mklmt10{_}2939{_}The captain of Number Nine was unconscious that he was holding his breath.
mklmt10{_}2940{_}He was oblivious of the man.
mklmt10{_}2941{_}It was the woman.
mklmt10{_}2942{_}Did she lose her head or courage, or misplay her muscular part for a moment, she could be hurled a hundred feet by that giant buffet and left wrenched, helpless, and breathless to be pulped on the coral bottom and sucked out by the undertow to be battened on by the fish-sharks too cowardly to take their human meat alive.
mklmt10{_}2943{_}Why didn't they dive deep, and with plenty of time, the captain wanted to know, instead of waiting till the last tick of safety and the first tick of peril were one?
mklmt10{_}2944{_}He saw the woman turn her head and laugh to the man, and his head turn in response.
mklmt10{_}2945{_}Above them, overhanging them, as they mounted the body of the wave, the beard, creaming white, then frothing into rose and gold, tossed upward into a spray of jewels.
mklmt10{_}2946{_}The crisp off-shore trade-wind caught the beard's fringes and blew them backward and upward yards and yards into the air.
mklmt10{_}2947{_}It was then, side by side, and six feet apart, that they dived straight under the over-curl even then disintegrating to chaos and falling.
mklmt10{_}2948{_}Like insects disappearing into the convolutions of some gorgeous gigantic orchid, so they disappeared, as beard and crest and spray and jewels, in many tons, crashed and thundered down just where they had disappeared the moment before, but where they were no longer.
mklmt10{_}2949{_}Beyond the wave they had gone through, they finally showed, side by side, still six feet apart, swimming shoreward with a steady stroke until the next wave should make them body-surf it or face and pierce it.
mklmt10{_}2950{_}The captain of Number Nine waved his hand to his crew in dismissal, and sat down on the lanai railing, feeling vaguely tired and still watching the swimmers through his glasses.
mklmt10{_}2951{_}"Whoever and whatever they are," he murmured, "they aren't malahinis.
mklmt10{_}2952{_}They simply can't be malahinis."
mklmt10{_}2953{_}Not all days, and only on rare days, is the surf heavy at Waikiki; and, in the days that followed, Ida and Lee Barton, much in evidence on the beach and in the water, continued to arouse disparaging interest in the breasts of the tourist ladies, although the Outrigger captains ceased from worrying about them in the water.
mklmt10{_}2954{_}They would watch the pair swim out and disappear in the blue distance, and they might, or might not, chance to see them return hours afterward.
mklmt10{_}2955{_}The point was that the captains did not bother about their returning, because they knew they would return.
mklmt10{_}2956{_}The reason for this was that they were not malahinis.
mklmt10{_}2957{_}They belonged.
mklmt10{_}2958{_}In other words, or, rather, in the potent Islands-word, they were kamaaina.
mklmt10{_}2959{_}Kamaaina men and women of forty remembered Lee Barton from their childhood days, when, in truth, he had been a malahini, though a very young specimen.
mklmt10{_}2960{_}Since that time, in the course of various long stays, he had earned the kamaaina distinction.
mklmt10{_}2961{_}As for Ida Barton, young matrons of her own age (privily wondering how she managed to keep her figure) met her with arms around and hearty Hawaiian kisses.
mklmt10{_}2962{_}Grandmothers must have her to tea and reminiscence in old gardens of forgotten houses which the tourist never sees.
mklmt10{_}2963{_}Less than a week after her arrival, the aged Queen Liliuokalani must send for her and chide her for neglect.
mklmt10{_}2964{_}And old men, on cool and balmy lanais, toothlessly maundered to her about Grandpa Captain Wilton, of before their time, but whose wild and lusty deeds and pranks, told them by their fathers, they remembered with gusto--Grandpa Captain Wilton, or David Wilton, or "All Hands" as the Hawaiians of that remote day had affectionately renamed him.
mklmt10{_}2965{_}All Hands, ex-Northwest trader, the godless, beach-combing, clipper-shipless and ship-wrecked skipper who had stood on the beach at Kailua and welcomed the very first of missionaries, off the brig Thaddeus, in the year 1820, and who, not many years later, made a scandalous runaway marriage with one of their daughters, quieted down and served the Kamehamehas long and conservatively as Minister of the Treasury and Chief of the Customs, and acted as intercessor and mediator between the missionaries on one side and the beach-combing crowd, the trading crowd, and the Hawaiian chiefs on the variously shifting other side.
mklmt10{_}2966{_}Nor was Lee Barton neglected.
mklmt10{_}2967{_}In the midst of the dinners and lunches, the luaus (Hawaiian feasts) and poi-suppers, and swims and dances in aloha (love) to both of them, his time and inclination were claimed by the crowd of lively youngsters of old Kohala days who had come to know that they possessed digestions and various other internal functions, and who had settled down to somewhat of sedateness, who roistered less, and who played bridge much, and went to baseball often.
mklmt10{_}2968{_}Also, similarly oriented, was the old poker crowd of Lee Barton's younger days, which crowd played for more consistent stakes and limits, while it drank mineral water and orange juice and timed the final round of "Jacks" never later than midnight.
mklmt10{_}2969{_}Appeared, through all the rout of entertainment, Sonny Grandison, Hawaii-born, Hawaii-prominent, who, despite his youthful forty-one years, had declined the proffered governorship of the Territory.
mklmt10{_}2970{_}Also, he had ducked Ida Barton in the surf at Waikiki a quarter of a century before, and, still earlier, vacationing on his father's great Lakanaii cattle ranch, had hair-raisingly initiated her, and various other tender tots of five to seven years of age, into his boys' band, "The Cannibal Head-Hunters" or "The Terrors of Lakanaii."
mklmt10{_}2971{_}Still farther, his Grandpa Grandison and her Grandpa Wilton had been business and political comrades in the old days.
mklmt10{_}2972{_}Educated at Harvard, he had become for a time a world-wandering scientist and social favourite.
mklmt10{_}2973{_}After serving in the Philippines, he had accompanied various expeditions through Malaysia, South America, and Africa in the post of official entomologist.
