mklmt10{_}2974{_}At forty-one he still retained his travelling commission from the Smithsonian Institution, while his friends insisted that he knew more about sugar "bugs" than the expert entomologists employed by him and his fellow sugar planters in the Experiment Station.
mklmt10{_}2975{_}Bulking large at home, he was the best-known representative of Hawaii abroad.
mklmt10{_}2976{_}It was the axiom among travelled Hawaii folk, that wherever over the world they might mention they were from Hawaii, the invariable first question asked of them was:  "And do you know Sonny Grandison?"
mklmt10{_}2977{_}In brief, he was a wealthy man's son who had made good.
mklmt10{_}2978{_}His father's million he inherited he had increased to ten millions, at the same time keeping up his father's benefactions and endowments and overshadowing them with his own.
mklmt10{_}2979{_}But there was still more to him.
mklmt10{_}2980{_}A ten years' widower, without issue, he was the most eligible and most pathetically sought-after marriageable man in all Hawaii.
mklmt10{_}2981{_}A clean-and-strong-featured brunette, tall, slenderly graceful, with the lean runner's stomach, always fit as a fiddle, a distinguished figure in any group, the greying of hair over his temples (in juxtaposition to his young- textured skin and bright vital eyes) made him appear even more distinguished.
mklmt10{_}2982{_}Despite the social demands upon his time, and despite his many committee meetings, and meetings of boards of directors and political conferences, he yet found time and space to captain the Lakanaii polo team to more than occasional victory, and on his own island of Lakanaii vied with the Baldwins of Maui in the breeding and importing of polo ponies.
mklmt10{_}2983{_}Given a markedly strong and vital man and woman, when a second equally markedly strong and vital man enters the scene, the peril of a markedly strong and vital triangle of tragedy becomes imminent.
mklmt10{_}2984{_}Indeed, such a triangle of tragedy may be described, in the terminology of the flat-floor folk, as "super" and "impossible."
mklmt10{_}2985{_}Perhaps, since within himself originated the desire and the daring, it was Sonny Grandison who first was conscious of the situation, although he had to be quick to anticipate the sensing intuition of a woman like Ida Barton.
mklmt10{_}2986{_}At any rate, and undebatable, the last of the three to attain awareness was Lee Barton, who promptly laughed away what was impossible to laugh away.
mklmt10{_}2987{_}His first awareness, he quickly saw, was so belated that half his hosts and hostesses were already aware.
mklmt10{_}2988{_}Casting back, he realized that for some time any affair to which he and his wife were invited found Sonny Grandison likewise invited.
mklmt10{_}2989{_}Wherever the two had been, the three had been.
mklmt10{_}2990{_}To Kahuku or to Haleiwa, to Ahuimanu, or to Kaneohe for the coral gardens, or to Koko Head for a picnicking and a swimming, somehow it invariably happened that Ida rode in Sonny's car or that both rode in somebody's car.
mklmt10{_}2991{_}Dances, luaus, dinners, and outings were all one; the three of them were there.
mklmt10{_}2992{_}Having become aware, Lee Barton could not fail to register Ida's note of happiness ever rising when in the same company with Sonny Grandison, and her willingness to ride in the same cars with him, to dance with him, or to sit out dances with him.
mklmt10{_}2993{_}Most convincing of all, was Sonny Grandison himself.
mklmt10{_}2994{_}Forty-one, strong, experienced, his face could no more conceal what he felt than could be concealed a lad of twenty's ordinary lad's love.
mklmt10{_}2995{_}Despite the control and restraint of forty years, he could no more mask his soul with his face than could Lee Barton, of equal years, fail to read that soul through so transparent a face.
mklmt10{_}2996{_}And often, to other women, talking, when the topic of Sonny came up, Lee Barton heard Ida express her fondness for Sonny, or her almost too-eloquent appreciation of his polo-playing, his work in the world, and his general all-rightness of achievement.
mklmt10{_}2997{_}About Sonny's state of mind and heart Lee had no doubt.
mklmt10{_}2998{_}It was patent enough for the world to read.
mklmt10{_}2999{_}But how about Ida, his own dozen-years' wife of a glorious love-match?
mklmt10{_}3000{_}He knew that woman, ever the mysterious sex, was capable any time of unguessed mystery.
mklmt10{_}3001{_}Did her frank comradeliness with Grandison token merely frank comradeliness and childhood contacts continued and recrudesced into adult years?
mklmt10{_}3002{_}or did it hide, in woman's subtler and more secretive ways, a beat of heart and return of feeling that might even out- balance what Sonny's face advertised?
mklmt10{_}3003{_}Lee Barton was not happy.
mklmt10{_}3004{_}A dozen years of utmost and post-nuptial possession of his wife had proved to him, so far as he was concerned, that she was his one woman in the world, and that the woman was unborn, much less unglimpsed, who could for a moment compete with her in his heart, his soul, and his brain.
mklmt10{_}3005{_}Impossible of existence was the woman who could lure him away from her, much less over-bid her in the myriad, continual satisfactions she rendered him.
mklmt10{_}3006{_}Was this, then, he asked himself, the dreaded contingency of all fond Benedicts, to be her first "affair?"
mklmt10{_}3007{_}He tormented himself with the ever iterant query, and, to the astonishment of the reformed Kohala poker crowd of wise and middle-aged youngsters as well as to the reward of the keen scrutiny of the dinner-giving and dinner-attending women, he began to drink King William instead of orange juice, to bully up the poker limit, to drive of nights his own car more than rather recklessly over the Pali and Diamond Head roads, and, ere dinner or lunch or after, to take more than an average man's due of old-fashioned cocktails and Scotch highs.
mklmt10{_}3008{_}All the years of their marriage she had been ever complaisant toward him in his card-playing.
mklmt10{_}3009{_}This complaisance, to him, had become habitual.
mklmt10{_}3010{_}But now that doubt had arisen, it seemed to him that he noted an eagerness in her countenancing of his poker parties.
mklmt10{_}3011{_}Another point he could not avoid noting was that Sonny Grandison was missed by the poker and bridge crowds.
mklmt10{_}3012{_}He seemed to be too busy.
mklmt10{_}3013{_}Now where was Sonny, while he, Lee Barton, was playing?
mklmt10{_}3014{_}Surely not always at committee and boards of directors meetings.
mklmt10{_}3015{_}Lee Barton made sure of this.
mklmt10{_}3016{_}He easily learned that at such times Sonny was more than usually wherever Ida chanced to be-- at dances, or dinners, or moonlight swimming parties, or, the very afternoon he had flatly pleaded rush of affairs as an excuse not to join Lee and Langhorne Jones and Jack Holstein in a bridge battle at the Pacific Club--that afternoon he had played bridge at Dora Niles' home with three women, one of whom was Ida.
mklmt10{_}3017{_}Returning, once, from an afternoon's inspection of the great dry- dock building at Pearl Harbour, Lee Barton, driving his machine against time, in order to have time to dress for dinner, passed Sonny's car; and Sonny's one passenger, whom he was taking home, was Ida.
mklmt10{_}3018{_}One night, a week later, during which interval he had played no cards, he came home at eleven from a stag dinner at the University Club, just preceding Ida's return from the Alstone poi supper and dance.
mklmt10{_}3019{_}And Sonny had driven her home.
mklmt10{_}3020{_}Major Fanklin and his wife had first been dropped off by them, they mentioned, at Fort Shafter, on the other side of town and miles away from the beach.
mklmt10{_}3021{_}Lee Barton, after all mere human man, as a human man unfailingly meeting Sonny in all friendliness, suffered poignantly in secret.
mklmt10{_}3022{_}Not even Ida dreamed that he suffered; and she went her merry, careless, laughing way, secure in her own heart, although a trifle perplexed at her husband's increase in number of pre-dinner cocktails.
mklmt10{_}3023{_}Apparently, as always, she had access to almost all of him; but now she did not have access to his unguessable torment, nor to the long parallel columns of mental book-keeping running their totalling balances from moment to moment, day and night, in his brain.
mklmt10{_}3024{_}In one column were her undoubtable spontaneous expressions of her usual love and care for him, her many acts of comfort-serving and of advice-asking and advice-obeying.
mklmt10{_}3025{_}In another column, in which the items increasingly were entered, were her expressions and acts which he could not but classify as dubious.
mklmt10{_}3026{_}Were they what they seemed?
mklmt10{_}3027{_}Or were they of duplicity compounded, whether deliberately or unconsciously?
mklmt10{_}3028{_}The third column, longest of all, totalling most in human heart-appraisements, was filled with items relating directly or indirectly to her and Sonny Grandison.
mklmt10{_}3029{_}Lee Barton did not deliberately do this book-keeping.
mklmt10{_}3030{_}He could not help it.
mklmt10{_}3031{_}He would have liked to avoid it.
mklmt10{_}3032{_}But in his fairly ordered mind the items of entry, of themselves and quite beyond will on his part, took their places automatically in their respective columns.
mklmt10{_}3033{_}In his distortion of vision, magnifying apparently trivial detail which half the time he felt he magnified, he had recourse to MacIlwaine, to whom he had once rendered a very considerable service.
mklmt10{_}3034{_}MacIlwaine was chief of detectives.
mklmt10{_}3035{_}"Is Sonny Grandison a womaning man?"
mklmt10{_}3036{_}Barton had demanded.
mklmt10{_}3037{_}MacIlwaine had said nothing.
mklmt10{_}3038{_}"Then he is a womaning man," had been Barton's declaration.
mklmt10{_}3039{_}And still the chief of detectives had said nothing.
mklmt10{_}3040{_}Briefly afterward, ere he destroyed it as so much dynamite, Lee Barton went over the written report.
mklmt10{_}3041{_}Not bad, not really bad, was the summarization; but not too good after the death of his wife ten years before.
mklmt10{_}3042{_}That had been a love-match almost notorious in Honolulu society, because of the completeness of infatuation, not only before, but after marriage, and up to her tragic death when her horse fell with her a thousand feet off Nahiku Trail.
mklmt10{_}3043{_}And not for a long time afterward, MacIlwaine stated, had Grandison been guilty of interest in any woman.
mklmt10{_}3044{_}And whatever it was, it had been unvaryingly decent.
mklmt10{_}3045{_}Never a hint of gossip or scandal; and the entire community had come to accept that he was a one-woman man, and would never marry again.
mklmt10{_}3046{_}What small affairs MacIlwaine had jotted down he insisted that Sonny Grandison did not dream were known by another person outside the principals themselves.
mklmt10{_}3047{_}Barton glanced hurriedly, almost shamedly, at the several names and incidents, and knew surprise ere he committed the document to the flames.
mklmt10{_}3048{_}At any rate, Sonny had been most discreet.
mklmt10{_}3049{_}As he stared at the ashes, Barton pondered how much of his own younger life, from his bachelor days, resided in old MacIlwaine's keeping.
mklmt10{_}3050{_}Next, Barton found himself blushing, to himself, at himself.
mklmt10{_}3051{_}If MacIlwaine knew so much of the private lives of community figures, then had not he, her husband and protector and shielder, planted in MacIlwaine's brain a suspicion of Ida?
mklmt10{_}3052{_}"Anything on your mind?"
mklmt10{_}3053{_}Lee asked his wife that evening, as he stood holding her wrap while she put the last touches to her dressing.
mklmt10{_}3054{_}This was in line with their old and successful compact of frankness, and he wondered, while he waited her answer, why he had refrained so long from asking her.
mklmt10{_}3055{_}"No," she smiled.
mklmt10{_}3056{_}"Nothing particular.
mklmt10{_}3057{_}Afterwards .
mklmt10{_}3058{_}.
mklmt10{_}3059{_}.
mklmt10{_}3060{_}perhaps .
mklmt10{_}3061{_}.
mklmt10{_}3062{_}. "
mklmt10{_}3063{_}She became absorbed in gazing at herself in the mirror, while she dabbed some powder on her nose and dabbed it off again.
mklmt10{_}3064{_}"You know my way, Lee," she added, after the pause.
mklmt10{_}3065{_}"It takes me time to gather things together in my own way--when there are things to gather; but when I do, you always get them.
mklmt10{_}3066{_}And often there's nothing in them after all, I find, and so you are saved the nuisance of them."
mklmt10{_}3067{_}She held out her arms for him to place the wrap about her--her valiant little arms that were so wise and steel-like in battling with the breakers, and that yet were such just mere-woman's arms, round and warm and white, delicious as a woman's arms should be, with the canny muscles, masking under soft-roundness of contour and fine smooth skin, capable of being flexed at will by the will of her.
mklmt10{_}3068{_}He pondered her, with a grievous hurt and yearning of appreciation- -so delicate she seemed, so porcelain-fragile that a strong man could snap her in the crook of his arm.
mklmt10{_}3069{_}"We must hurry!"
mklmt10{_}3070{_}she cried, as he lingered in the adjustment of the flimsy wrap over her flimsy-prettiness of gown.
mklmt10{_}3071{_}"We'll be late.
mklmt10{_}3072{_}And if it showers up Nuuanu, putting the curtains up will make us miss the second dance."
mklmt10{_}3073{_}He made a note to observe with whom she danced that second dance, as she preceded him across the room to the door; while at the same time he pleasured his eye in what he had so often named to himself as the spirit-proud flesh-proud walk of her.
mklmt10{_}3074{_}"You don't feel I'm neglecting you in my too-much poker?"
mklmt10{_}3075{_}he tried again, by indirection.
mklmt10{_}3076{_}"Mercy, no!
mklmt10{_}3077{_}You know I just love you to have your card orgies.
mklmt10{_}3078{_}They're tonic for you.
mklmt10{_}3079{_}And you're so much nicer about them, so much more middle-aged.
mklmt10{_}3080{_}Why, it's almost years since you sat up later than one."
mklmt10{_}3081{_}It did not shower up Nuuanu, and every overhead star was out in a clear trade-wind sky.

mklmt10{_}3083{_}An hour later, depressed and restless, declining to make one of a bridge foursome in the library and escaping from a few young matrons, he strolled out into the generous grounds.
mklmt10{_}3084{_}Across the lawn, at the far edge, he came upon the hedge of night-blooming cereus.
mklmt10{_}3085{_}To each flower, opening after dark and fading, wilting, perishing with the dawn, this was its one night of life.
mklmt10{_}3086{_}The great, cream-white blooms, a foot in diameter and more, lily-like and wax-like, white beacons of attraction in the dark, penetrating and seducing the night with their perfume, were busy and beautiful with their brief glory of living.
mklmt10{_}3087{_}But the way along the hedge was populous with humans, two by two, male and female, stealing out between the dances or strolling the dances out, while they talked in low soft voices and gazed upon the wonder of flower-love.
mklmt10{_}3088{_}From the lanai drifted the love-caressing strains of "Hanalei" sung by the singing boys.
mklmt10{_}3089{_}Vaguely Lee Barton remembered--perhaps it was from some Maupassant story--the abbe, obsessed by the theory that behind all things were the purposes of God and perplexed so to interpret the night, who discovered at the last that the night was ordained for love.
mklmt10{_}3090{_}The unanimity of the night as betrayed by flowers and humans was a hurt to Barton.
mklmt10{_}3091{_}He circled back toward the house along a winding path that skirted within the edge of shadow of the monkey-pods and algaroba trees.
mklmt10{_}3092{_}In the obscurity, where his path curved away into the open again, he looked across a space of a few feet where, on another path in the shadow, stood a pair in each other's arms.
mklmt10{_}3093{_}The impassioned low tones of the man had caught his ear and drawn his eyes, and at the moment of his glance, aware of his presence, the voice ceased, and the two remained immobile, furtive, in each other's arms.
mklmt10{_}3094{_}He continued his walk, sombred by the thought that in the gloom of the trees was the next progression from the openness of the sky over those who strolled the night-flower hedge.
mklmt10{_}3095{_}Oh, he knew the game when of old no shadow was too deep, no ruse of concealment too furtive, to veil a love moment.
mklmt10{_}3096{_}After all, humans were like flowers, he meditated.

mklmt10{_}3099{_}Bursting into its bloom after the dawn, snow-white, warming to pink under the hours of sun, and quickening to scarlet with the dark from which its beauty and its being would never emerge, it seemed to him that it epitomized man's life and passion.

mklmt10{_}3343{_}.
mklmt10{_}3344{_}.
mklmt10{_}3345{_}it was his renunciation.
mklmt10{_}3346{_}And I didn't love Sonny.
mklmt10{_}3347{_}I don't love him.
mklmt10{_}3348{_}I have loved you, and you only, all the time."
mklmt10{_}3349{_}She waited, and felt her husband's arm pass around her shoulder and under her own arm, and yielded to his drawing down of her to him.
mklmt10{_}3350{_}"You did have me worried more than a bit," he admitted, "until I was afraid I was going to lose you.
mklmt10{_}3351{_}And .
mklmt10{_}3352{_}.
mklmt10{_}3353{_}. "
mklmt10{_}3354{_}He broke off in patent embarrassment, then gripped the idea courageously.
mklmt10{_}3355{_}"Oh, well, you know you're my one woman.
mklmt10{_}3356{_}Enough said."
mklmt10{_}3357{_}She fumbled the match-box from his pocket and struck a match to enable him to light his long-extinct cigar.
mklmt10{_}3358{_}"Well," he said, as the smoke curled about them, "knowing you as I know you, and ALL of you, all I can say is that I'm sorry for Sonny for what he's missed--awfully sorry for him, but equally glad for me.
mklmt10{_}3359{_}And .
mklmt10{_}3360{_}.
mklmt10{_}3361{_}.
mklmt10{_}3362{_}one other thing:  five years hence I've something to tell you, something rich, something ridiculously rich, and all about me and the foolishness of me over you.
mklmt10{_}3363{_}Five years.
mklmt10{_}3364{_}Is it a date?"
mklmt10{_}3365{_}"I shall keep it if it is fifty years," she sighed, as she nestled closer to him.
